margin: 0"> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Anjou" title="Anjou"><img alt="Anjou" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/France_anjou.svg/23px-France_anjou.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/France_anjou.svg/35px-France_anjou.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/France_anjou.svg/45px-France_anjou.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="217" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Anjou" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Anjou">Count of Anjou</a>\n</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Maine_flag.svg/23px-Maine_flag.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Maine_flag.svg/35px-Maine_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Maine_flag.svg/46px-Maine_flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="216" /></span> <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Maine" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Maine">Count of Maine</a>\n</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes"><img alt="Nantes" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nantes.svg/23px-Nantes.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nantes.svg/35px-Nantes.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nantes.svg/45px-Nantes.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="532" data-file-height="355" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Nantes" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Nantes">Count of Nantes</a>\n</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Poitou" title="Poitou"><img alt="Poitou" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Poitou.svg/23px-Flag_of_Poitou.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Poitou.svg/35px-Flag_of_Poitou.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Poitou.svg/45px-Flag_of_Poitou.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Poitou" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Poitou">Count of Poitou</a>\n</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Cyprus" title="Kingdom of Cyprus"><img alt="Kingdom of Cyprus" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Royal_banner_of_Janus_of_Cyprus.svg/15px-Royal_banner_of_Janus_of_Cyprus.svg.png" width="15" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Royal_banner_of_Janus_of_Cyprus.svg/23px-Royal_banner_of_Janus_of_Cyprus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Royal_banner_of_Janus_of_Cyprus.svg/30px-Royal_banner_of_Janus_of_Cyprus.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England#Conquest_of_Cyprus" title="Richard I of England">Lord of Cyprus</a>\n</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Dissolution</th><td>\n<div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li>1499 (male)</li>\n<li>1541 (female)</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Deposition</th><td>\n1485<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="dtend">1485</span>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Cadet branches</th><td>\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border: none; padding: 0;">\n<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left;">List</div>\n<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align: left; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lancaster" title="House of Lancaster">House of Lancaster</a>\n</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <a href="/wiki/House_of_York" title="House of York">House of York</a>\n</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>House of Plantagenet</b><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="/d\xca\x92/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">d\xca\x92</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>) was a <a href="/wiki/Royal_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal house">royal house</a> which originated from the lands of <a href="/wiki/Anjou" title="Anjou">Anjou</a> in France. The name Plantagenet is used by modern historians to identify four distinct royal houses: the <a href="/wiki/Angevin_kings_of_England" title="Angevin kings of England">Angevins</a>, who were also Counts of Anjou; the main body of the Plantagenets following the loss of Anjou; and the Plantagenets\' two <a href="/wiki/Cadet_branch" title="Cadet branch">cadet branches</a>, the Houses of <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lancaster" title="House of Lancaster">Lancaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_of_York" title="House of York">York</a>.  The family held the <a href="/wiki/English_throne" class="mw-redirect" title="English throne">English throne</a> from 1154, with the accession of <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">Henry II</a>, until 1485, when <a href="/wiki/Richard_III_of_England" title="Richard III of England">Richard III</a> died in battle.\n</p><p>Under the Plantagenets, England was transformed &#8211; although this was only partly intentional. The Plantagenet kings were often forced to negotiate compromises such as <a href="/wiki/Magna_Carta" title="Magna Carta">Magna Carta</a>. These constrained royal power in return for financial and military support. The king was no longer just the most powerful man in the nation, holding the prerogative of judgement, feudal tribute and warfare. He now had defined duties to the realm, underpinned by a sophisticated justice system. A distinct national identity was shaped by conflict with the French, Scots, Welsh and Irish, and the establishment of English as the primary language.\n</p><p>In the 15th century, the Plantagenets were defeated in the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years&#39; War">Hundred Years\' War</a> and beset with social, political and economic problems. Popular revolts were commonplace, triggered by the denial of numerous freedoms.  English nobles raised private armies, engaged in private feuds and openly defied <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">Henry VI</a>.\n</p><p>The rivalry between the House of Plantagenet\'s two cadet branches of York and Lancaster brought about the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a>, a decades-long fight for the English succession, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bosworth_Field" title="Battle of Bosworth Field">Battle of Bosworth Field</a> in 1485, when the reign of the Plantagenets and the <a href="/wiki/England_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="England in the Middle Ages">English Middle Ages</a> both met their end with the death of King Richard III. <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII</a>, of Lancastrian descent, became king of England; five months later, he married <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_York" title="Elizabeth of York">Elizabeth of York</a>, thus ending the Wars of the Roses, and giving rise to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Tudor" title="House of Tudor">Tudor dynasty</a>. The Tudors worked to centralise English royal power, which allowed them to avoid some of the problems that had plagued the last Plantagenet rulers. The resulting stability allowed for the <a href="/wiki/English_Renaissance" title="English Renaissance">English Renaissance</a>, and the advent of <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_Britain" title="Early modern Britain">early modern Britain</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Tudor"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Tudor</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#De_La_Pole"><span class="toctext">Pole</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Stafford"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Stafford</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Tudor_succession"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Tudor succession</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a class="toctext">Notes</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plantagenet"><i>Plantagenet</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Plantagenet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_II_Plantagenet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ancient depiction of the first Plantagenet King Henry the 2nd of England" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Henry_II_Plantagenet.jpg/170px-Henry_II_Plantagenet.jpg" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/Henry_II_Plantagenet.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="207" data-file-height="368" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_II_Plantagenet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">Henry II</a> (1154-1189) is considered by some to be the first Plantagenet king of England.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Richard_of_York,_3rd_Duke_of_York" title="Richard of York, 3rd Duke of York">Richard of York, 3rd Duke of York</a>, adopted Plantagenet as his family name in the 15th century. <i>Plantegenest</i> (or <i>Plante Genest</i>) had been a 12th-century nickname for his ancestor <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Plantagenet,_Count_of_Anjou" title="Geoffrey Plantagenet, Count of Anjou">Geoffrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Anjou" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Anjou">Count of Anjou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Normandy" title="Duke of Normandy">Duke of Normandy</a>. One of many popular theories suggests the <a href="/wiki/Cytisus_scoparius" title="Cytisus scoparius">common broom</a>, <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">planta <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/genista" class="extiw" title="wikt:genista">genista</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Latin" title="Medieval Latin">medieval Latin</a>, as the source of the nickname.<sup id="cite_ref-plant2007_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plant2007-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It is uncertain why Richard chose this specific name, although during the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a> it emphasised Richard\'s status as Geoffrey\'s patrilineal descendant. The retrospective usage of the name for all of Geoffrey\'s male descendants was popular during the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Tudor_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Tudor dynasty">Tudor dynasty</a>, perhaps encouraged by the further legitimacy it gave to Richard\'s great-grandson, <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry VIII">Henry VIII</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> It was only in the late 17th century that it passed into common usage among historians.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilson_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angevins"><i>Angevins</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Angevins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Angevin_kings_of_England" title="Angevin kings of England">Angevin kings of England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angevin_Empire" title="Angevin Empire">Angevin Empire</a></div>\n<p><i lang="fr"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Angevin#French" class="extiw" title="wikt:Angevin">Angevin</a></i> is French for "from <a href="/wiki/Anjou" title="Anjou">Anjou</a>". The three Angevin kings were <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">Henry II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard I</a> and <a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">John</a>. "Angevin" can also refer to the period of history in which they reigned. Many historians identify the Angevins as a distinct English royal house. "Angevin" is also used in reference to any sovereign or government derived from Anjou. As a noun, it refers to any native of Anjou or an Angevin ruler, and specifically to other <a href="/wiki/Counts_and_dukes_of_Anjou" title="Counts and dukes of Anjou">counts and dukes of Anjou</a>, including the ancestors of the three kings who formed the English royal house; their cousins, who held the crown of <a href="/wiki/King_of_Jerusalem#House_of_Anjou" title="King of Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>; and to unrelated members of the French royal family who were later granted the titles and formed different dynasties, such as the <a href="/wiki/Capetian_House_of_Anjou" title="Capetian House of Anjou">Capetian House of Anjou</a> and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Valois-Anjou" title="House of Valois-Anjou">Valois House of Anjou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, there is disagreement between those who consider <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_England" title="Henry III of England">Henry III</a> to be the first Plantagenet monarch, and those who do not distinguish between Angevins and Plantagenets and therefore consider the first Plantagenet to be Henry II.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The term "Angevin Empire" was coined by <a href="/wiki/Kate_Norgate" title="Kate Norgate">Kate Norgate</a> in 1887. There was no known contemporary collective name for all of the territories under the rule of the Angevin Kings of England.  This led to circumlocutions such as "our kingdom and everything subject to our rule whatever it may be" or "the whole of the kingdom which had belonged to his father". The "Empire" portion of "Angevin Empire" has been controversial, especially as these territories were not subject to any unified laws or systems of governance, and each retained its own laws, traditions, and feudal relationships.  In 1986 a convention of historians concluded that there had not been an Angevin state, and therefore no "<a href="/wiki/Angevin_Empire" title="Angevin Empire">Angevin Empire</a>", but that the term <i lang="fr" title="French language text">espace Plantagenet</i> (French for "Plantagenet area") was acceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, historians have continued to use "Angevin Empire".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;nb 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">Origin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Origin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Children_of_Henry2_England.jpg" class="image"><img alt="An illuminated diagram showing the Angevins; coloured lines connect the two to show the lineal descent" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/The_Children_of_Henry2_England.jpg/310px-The_Children_of_Henry2_England.jpg" width="310" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/The_Children_of_Henry2_England.jpg/465px-The_Children_of_Henry2_England.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/The_Children_of_Henry2_England.jpg/620px-The_Children_of_Henry2_England.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2122" data-file-height="969" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Children_of_Henry2_England.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>13th-century depiction of Henry II and his legitimate children: <a href="/wiki/William_IX,_Count_of_Poitiers" title="William IX, Count of Poitiers">William</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Young_King" title="Henry the Young King">Henry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matilda_of_England,_Duchess_of_Saxony" title="Matilda of England, Duchess of Saxony">Matilda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_II,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Geoffrey II, Duke of Brittany">Geoffrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_England,_Queen_of_Castile" title="Eleanor of England, Queen of Castile">Eleanor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_of_England,_Queen_of_Sicily" title="Joan of England, Queen of Sicily">Joan</a> and <a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">John</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The later <a href="/wiki/Counts_of_Anjou" class="mw-redirect" title="Counts of Anjou">counts of Anjou</a>, including the Plantagenets, descended from <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_II,_Count_of_G%C3%A2tinais" title="Geoffrey II, Count of G\xc3\xa2tinais">Geoffrey II, Count of G\xc3\xa2tinais</a>, and his wife <a href="/wiki/Ermengarde_of_Anjou,_Duchess_of_Burgundy" title="Ermengarde of Anjou, Duchess of Burgundy">Ermengarde of Anjou</a>. In 1060 the couple inherited the title via <a href="/wiki/Cognatic_kinship" title="Cognatic kinship">cognatic kinship</a> from <a href="/wiki/House_of_Ingelger" title="House of Ingelger">an Angevin family</a> that was descended from a noble named <a href="/wiki/Ingelger" title="Ingelger">Ingelger</a>, whose recorded history dates from 870.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies190_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies190-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 10th and 11th centuries, power struggles occurred between rulers in northern and western France including those of Anjou, <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poitou" title="Poitou">Poitou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blois" title="Blois">Blois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maine_(province)" title="Maine (province)">Maine</a>, and the kings of France. In the early 12th century Geoffrey of Anjou married <a href="/wiki/Empress_Matilda" title="Empress Matilda">Empress Matilda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_England" title="Henry I of England">King Henry I</a>\'s only surviving legitimate child and heir to the English throne. As a result of this marriage, Geoffrey\'s son <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">Henry II</a> inherited the English throne as well as Norman and Angevin titles, thus marking the beginning of the Angevin and Plantagenet dynasties.<sup id="cite_ref-Gillingham7_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gillingham7-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The marriage was the third attempt of Geoffrey\'s father, <a href="/wiki/Fulk_V,_Count_of_Anjou" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulk V, Count of Anjou">Fulk V, Count of Anjou</a>, to build a political alliance with Normandy. He first espoused his daughter, <a href="/wiki/Matilda_of_Anjou" title="Matilda of Anjou">Alice</a>, to <a href="/wiki/William_Adelin" title="William Adelin">William Adelin</a>, Henry I\'s heir. After William drowned in the wreck of the <i><a href="/wiki/White_Ship" title="White Ship">White Ship</a></i> Fulk married another of his daughters, <a href="/wiki/Sibylla_of_Anjou" title="Sibylla of Anjou">Sibylla</a>, to <a href="/wiki/William_Clito" title="William Clito">William Clito</a>, son of Henry I\'s older brother, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Curthose" title="Robert Curthose">Robert Curthose</a>. Henry I had the marriage annulled to avoid strengthening William\'s rival claim to Normandy. Finally Fulk achieved his goal through the marriage of Geoffrey and Matilda. Fulk then passed his titles to Geoffrey and became <a href="/wiki/King_of_Jerusalem" title="King of Jerusalem">King of Jerusalem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies1999p309_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies1999p309-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Angevin_kings">Angevin kings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Angevin kings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Angevin_kings_of_England" title="Angevin kings of England">Angevin kings of England</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrival_in_England">Arrival in England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Arrival in England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/The_Anarchy" title="The Anarchy">The Anarchy</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:France_1154-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of King Henry the second&#39;s continental holdings in 1154, covering parts of today&#39;s France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/France_1154-en.svg/220px-France_1154-en.svg.png" width="220" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/France_1154-en.svg/330px-France_1154-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/France_1154-en.svg/440px-France_1154-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1405" data-file-height="1675" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:France_1154-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">Henry II</a>\'s continental holdings in 1154, forming part of the "<a href="/wiki/Angevin_Empire" title="Angevin Empire">Angevin Empire</a>"</div></div></div>\n<p>When Henry II was born in 1133, his grandfather, Henry I, was reportedly delighted, saying that the boy was "the heir to the kingdom".<sup id="cite_ref-Gillingham_2001_11\xe2\x80\x9312_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gillingham_2001_11\xe2\x80\x9312-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The birth reduced the risk that the king\'s realm would pass to his son-in-law\'s family, which might have occurred if the marriage of Matilda and Geoffrey had proved childless. The birth of a second son, also named <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey,_Count_of_Nantes" title="Geoffrey, Count of Nantes">Geoffrey</a>, increased the likelihood that, in accordance with French custom, Henry would receive the English maternal inheritance and Geoffrey the Angevin paternal inheritance. This would separate the realms of England and Anjou.<sup id="cite_ref-Gillingham_2001_11\xe2\x80\x9312_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gillingham_2001_11\xe2\x80\x9312-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In order to secure an orderly succession, Geoffrey and Matilda sought more power from Henry I, but quarrelled with him after the king refused to give them power that might be used against him. When he died in December 1135, the couple were in Anjou, allowing Matilda\'s cousin <a href="/wiki/Stephen,_King_of_England" title="Stephen, King of England">Stephen</a> to seize the crown of England. Stephen\'s contested accession initiated the widespread civil unrest later called the Anarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-Schama2000p117_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schama2000p117-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Count Geoffrey had little interest in England. Instead he commenced a ten-year war for the duchy of Normandy, but it became clear that to bring this conflict to a successful conclusion Stephen would need to be challenged in England so in 1139 Matilda and her half-brother, <a href="/wiki/Robert,_1st_Earl_of_Gloucester" title="Robert, 1st Earl of Gloucester">Robert</a> invaded England.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> From the age of nine, Henry was repeatedly sent to England to be the male figurehead of the campaigns, since it became apparent that he would become king if England was conquered. In 1141 Stephen was captured at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lincoln_(1141)" title="Battle of Lincoln (1141)">Battle of Lincoln</a> and later exchanged for Robert who had also been captured.  Geoffrey continued the conquest of Normandy and in 1150 transferred the duchy to Henry while retaining the primary role in the duchy\'s government.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Three events allowed the Angevins\' successful termination of the conflict:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Count Geoffrey died in 1151 before finalizing the division of his realm between Henry and Henry\'s younger brother Geoffrey, who would have inherited Anjou. According to <a href="/wiki/William_of_Newburgh" title="William of Newburgh">William of Newburgh</a>, who wrote in the 1190s, Count Geoffrey decided that Henry would receive England and Anjou for as long as he needed the resources for the conflict against Stephen. Count Geoffrey instructed that his body should not be buried until Henry swore an oath that the young Geoffrey would receive Anjou when England and Normandy were secured.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/W._L._Warren" title="W. L. Warren">W. L. Warren</a> cast doubt on this account on the grounds that it was written later based on a single contemporary source, it would be questionable that either Geoffrey or Henry would consider such an oath binding and it would break the inheritance practice of the time.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The young Geoffrey died in 1158, before receiving Anjou, but he had become <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Nantes" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Nantes">count of Nantes</a> when the citizens of Nantes rebelled against their ruler. Henry had supported the rebellion.<sup id="cite_ref-Gillingham_2001_21_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gillingham_2001_21-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Louis_VII_of_France" title="Louis VII of France">Louis VII of France</a> was granted an annulment of his marriage to <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Aquitaine" title="Eleanor of Aquitaine">Eleanor of Aquitaine</a> on 18 March 1152, and she married Henry (who would become Henry II) on 18 May 1152. Consequently, the Angevins acquired the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Aquitaine" title="Duchy of Aquitaine">Duchy of Aquitaine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Stephen\'s wife and elder son, <a href="/wiki/Eustace_IV,_Count_of_Boulogne" title="Eustace IV, Count of Boulogne">Eustace</a>,  died in 1153 leading to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Wallingford" title="Treaty of Wallingford">Treaty of Wallingford</a>. The treaty agreed the peace offer that Matilda had rejected in 1142, recognised Henry as Stephen\'s heir, guaranteed Stephen\'s second son <a href="/wiki/William_I,_Count_of_Boulogne" title="William I, Count of Boulogne">William</a> his father\'s estates and allowed Stephen to be king for life. Stephen died soon afterwards, and Henry acceded to the throne in late 1154.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angevin_zenith">Angevin zenith</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Angevin zenith">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Of Henry\'s siblings, <a href="/wiki/William_FitzEmpress" title="William FitzEmpress">William</a> and Geoffrey died unmarried and childless, but the tempestuous marriage of Henry and Eleanor, who already had two daughters (<a href="/wiki/Marie_of_France,_Countess_of_Champagne" title="Marie of France, Countess of Champagne">Marie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alix_of_France" title="Alix of France">Alix</a>) through her first marriage to King Louis, produced eight children in thirteen years:<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/William_IX,_Count_of_Poitiers" title="William IX, Count of Poitiers">William IX, Count of Poitiers</a> (1153\xe2\x80\x931156)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Young_King" title="Henry the Young King">Henry the Young King</a> (1155\xe2\x80\x931183)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Matilda_of_England,_Duchess_of_Saxony" title="Matilda of England, Duchess of Saxony">Matilda, Duchess of Saxony</a> (1156\xe2\x80\x931189)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Lion" title="Henry the Lion">Henry the Lion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Bavaria">Duke of Bavaria</a>. The eldest amongst the couple\'s children, Richenza, is probably the daughter English chroniclers call Matilda, who was left in Normandy with her grandparents in 1185 and married firstly to Geoffrey, <a href="/wiki/Lords,_counts_and_dukes_of_Perche" title="Lords, counts and dukes of Perche">count of Perche</a>, and secondly to <a href="/wiki/Enguerrand_III,_Lord_of_Coucy" title="Enguerrand III, Lord of Coucy">Enguerrand de Coucy</a>. The eldest son, <a href="/wiki/Henry_V,_Count_Palatine_of_the_Rhine" title="Henry V, Count Palatine of the Rhine">Henry</a>, became <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Saxony#Dukes_of_Saxony" title="List of rulers of Saxony">duke of Saxony</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_the_Electoral_Palatinate" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rulers of the Electoral Palatinate">count palatine of the Rhine</a>. His brother Otto was nominated by his uncle Richard I as <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_York" title="Earl of York">earl of York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Poitiers" title="Count of Poitiers">count of Poitiers</a> before being elected <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">emperor</a> in opposition to the <a href="/wiki/Hohenstaufen" title="Hohenstaufen">Hohenstaufen</a> candidate. Otto was crowned in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> but he was later excommunicated and declared deposed. Childless, Otto lost power following the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Welf" title="House of Welf">Welf</a> and Angevin forces at the Battle of Bouvines. The youngest child, <a href="/wiki/William_of_Winchester,_Lord_of_L%C3%BCneburg" class="mw-redirect" title="William of Winchester, Lord of L\xc3\xbcneburg">William of Winchester</a> married <a href="/wiki/Helena_of_Denmark" title="Helena of Denmark">Helena</a> daughter of <a href="/wiki/Valdemar_I_of_Denmark" title="Valdemar I of Denmark">Valdemar I of Denmark</a>. Their only son, <a href="/wiki/Otto_I,_Duke_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" title="Otto I, Duke of Brunswick-L\xc3\xbcneburg">also called Otto</a>, was the sole male heir of his uncle Henry. The ducal house of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" title="Duchy of Brunswick-L\xc3\xbcneburg">Brunswick-L\xc3\xbcneburg</a> and the British royal <a href="/wiki/House_of_Windsor" title="House of Windsor">house of Windsor</a> both descend from him.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard I, King of England</a> (1157\xe2\x80\x931199). He had no legitimate offspring, but is thought to have had two illegitimate sons, of whom little is known, called Fulk and Phillip, Lord of Cognac.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_II,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Geoffrey II, Duke of Brittany">Geoffrey II, Duke of Brittany</a> (1158\xe2\x80\x931186)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Constance,_Duchess_of_Brittany" title="Constance, Duchess of Brittany">Constance</a> daughter of <a href="/wiki/Conan_IV,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Conan IV, Duke of Brittany">Duke Conan</a> of Brittany and became duke of Brittany by right of his wife. The couple\'s son Arthur was a competitor to John for the Angevin succession.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_England,_Queen_of_Castile" title="Eleanor of England, Queen of Castile">Eleanor, Queen of Castile</a> (1161\xe2\x80\x931214)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_VIII_of_Castile" title="Alfonso VIII of Castile">King Alfonso VIII of Castile</a>. The couple\'s children included <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_Castile" title="Henry I of Castile">King Henry of Castile</a> and four queen consorts, Berengaria, Queen of Leon, Urraca, Queen of Portugal, Blanche, Queen of France and Eleanor, Queen of Aragon.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joan_of_England,_Queen_of_Sicily" title="Joan of England, Queen of Sicily">Joan, Queen of Sicily</a> (1165\xe2\x80\x931199)\xe2\x80\x94married firstly <a href="/wiki/William_II_of_Sicily" title="William II of Sicily">King William II of Sicily</a> and secondly <a href="/wiki/Raymond_VI,_Count_of_Toulouse" title="Raymond VI, Count of Toulouse">Count Raymond VI of Toulouse</a>. Her children included <a href="/wiki/Raymond_VII,_Count_of_Toulouse" title="Raymond VII, Count of Toulouse">Raymond VII of Toulouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Weir_2008_65_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weir_2008_65-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">John, King of England</a> (1166\xe2\x80\x931216)</li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:English_-_Martyrdom_of_Saint_Thomas_Becket_-_Walters_W3415V_-_Open_Reverse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Miniature from an English psalter presenting a representation of the murder of Archbishop Becket" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/English_-_Martyrdom_of_Saint_Thomas_Becket_-_Walters_W3415V_-_Open_Reverse.jpg/170px-English_-_Martyrdom_of_Saint_Thomas_Becket_-_Walters_W3415V_-_Open_Reverse.jpg" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/English_-_Martyrdom_of_Saint_Thomas_Becket_-_Walters_W3415V_-_Open_Reverse.jpg/255px-English_-_Martyrdom_of_Saint_Thomas_Becket_-_Walters_W3415V_-_Open_Reverse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/English_-_Martyrdom_of_Saint_Thomas_Becket_-_Walters_W3415V_-_Open_Reverse.jpg/340px-English_-_Martyrdom_of_Saint_Thomas_Becket_-_Walters_W3415V_-_Open_Reverse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1292" data-file-height="1800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:English_-_Martyrdom_of_Saint_Thomas_Becket_-_Walters_W3415V_-_Open_Reverse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Miniature from an English <a href="/wiki/Psalter" title="Psalter">psalter</a> presenting a spirited account of the murder of Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Becket" title="Thomas Becket">Becket</a>, c. 1250, <a href="/wiki/Walters_Art_Museum" title="Walters Art Museum">Walters Art Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Henry also had illegitimate children with several mistresses, possibly as many as twelve. These children included <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_(archbishop_of_York)" title="Geoffrey (archbishop of York)">Geoffrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Longesp%C3%A9e,_3rd_Earl_of_Salisbury" title="William Longesp\xc3\xa9e, 3rd Earl of Salisbury">William</a>, Peter and four children who died young by <a href="/wiki/Alys_of_France,_Countess_of_Vexin" title="Alys of France, Countess of Vexin">Alys</a>, the daughter of Louis VII, while she was betrothed to his son Richard.<sup id="cite_ref-Weir_2008_65_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weir_2008_65-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> William\xe2\x80\x99s many competencies and importance as a royal bastard led to a long and illustrious career.<sup id="cite_ref-Longespee_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Longespee-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Henry reasserted and extended previous suzerainties to secure possession of his inherited realm.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In 1162 he attempted to re-establish what he saw as his authority over the English Church by appointing his friend <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Becket" title="Thomas Becket">Thomas Becket</a> as <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a> upon the death of the incumbent archbishop, <a href="/wiki/Theobald_of_Bec" title="Theobald of Bec">Theobald</a>. Becket\'s defiance as Archbishop alienated the king and his counsellors. Henry and Becket had repeated disputes over issues such as church tenures, the marriage of Henry\'s brother, and taxation. Henry reacted by getting Becket and other English bishops to recognise sixteen ancient customs in writing for the first time in the <a href="/wiki/Constitutions_of_Clarendon" title="Constitutions of Clarendon">Constitutions of Clarendon</a>, governing relations between the king, his courts and the church. When Becket tried to leave the country without permission, Henry tried to ruin him by filing legal cases relating to Becket\'s previous tenure as chancellor. Becket fled and remained in exile for five years. Relations later improved, and Becket returned, but they declined again when Henry\'s son was crowned as <a href="/wiki/Coregent" class="mw-redirect" title="Coregent">coregent</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_York" title="Archbishop of York">Archbishop of York</a>, which Becket perceived as a challenge to his authority. Becket later excommunicated those who had offended him. When he received this news, Henry said: "What miserable drones and traitors have I nurtured and promoted in my household who let their lord be treated with such shameful contempt by a low-born clerk." Four of Henry\'s knights killed Becket in <a href="/wiki/Canterbury_Cathedral" title="Canterbury Cathedral">Canterbury Cathedral</a> after Becket resisted a failed arrest attempt. Henry was widely considered complicit in Becket\'s death throughout Christian Europe. This made Henry a pariah; in penance, he walked barefoot into Canterbury Cathedral, where he was severely whipped by monks.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nFrom 1155 Henry claimed that <a href="/wiki/Pope_Adrian_IV" title="Pope Adrian IV">Pope Adrian IV</a> had given him authorisation to reform the Irish church by assuming control of Ireland, but Professor Anne Duggan\'s research indicates that the <a href="/wiki/Laudabiliter" title="Laudabiliter">Laudabiliter</a> is a falsification of an existing letter and that was not in fact Adrian\'s intention.<sup id="cite_ref-Ireland_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ireland-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> It originally allowed Henry\'s brother William some territory. Henry did not personally act on this until 1171 by which time William was already dead. He invaded Ireland to assert his authority over knights who had accrued autonomous power after they recruited soldiers in England and Wales and colonised Ireland with his permission. Henry later gave Ireland to his youngest son, John.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In 1172 Henry gave John the castles of <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Chinon" title="Ch\xc3\xa2teau de Chinon">Chinon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loudun" title="Loudun">Loudun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirebeau" title="Mirebeau">Mirebeau</a> as a wedding gift. This angered Henry\'s eighteen-year-old son, <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Young_King" title="Henry the Young King">Henry the Young King</a>, who believed these were his. A <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_1173%E2%80%931174" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolt of 1173\xe2\x80\x931174">rebellion</a> by Henry II\'s wife and three eldest sons ensued. <a href="/wiki/Louis_VII_of_France" title="Louis VII of France">Louis VII of France</a> supported the rebellion. <a href="/wiki/William_the_Lion" title="William the Lion">William the Lion</a>, king of the Scots, and others joined the revolt. After eighteen months, Henry subdued the rebels.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seal_-_Richard_I_of_England.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of the 1195 seal of Richard I of England. Exhibited in the History Museum of Vendee" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Seal_-_Richard_I_of_England.jpg/220px-Seal_-_Richard_I_of_England.jpg" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Seal_-_Richard_I_of_England.jpg/330px-Seal_-_Richard_I_of_England.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Seal_-_Richard_I_of_England.jpg/440px-Seal_-_Richard_I_of_England.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2990" data-file-height="2867" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seal_-_Richard_I_of_England.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard I</a>\'s Great Seal of 1189; the History Museum of Vendee</div></div></div><p> In <a href="/wiki/Le_Mans" title="Le Mans">Le Mans</a> in 1182, Henry II gathered his children to plan a <a href="/wiki/Partible_inheritance" title="Partible inheritance">partible inheritance</a>: his eldest surviving son, Henry, would inherit England, Normandy and Anjou; Richard (his mother\'s favourite) would inherit the Duchy of Aquitaine; <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_II,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Geoffrey II, Duke of Brittany">Geoffrey</a> would inherit Brittany; and John would inherit Ireland.  This resulted in further conflict. The younger Henry rebelled again, but died of <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a>. Geoffrey died in 1186 after an accident in a tournament. In 1189, Richard and <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_France" title="Philip II of France">Philip II of France</a> reasserted their various claims exploiting the aging Henry\'s failing health. Henry was forced to accept humiliating peace terms, including naming Richard his sole heir. The old King died two days later, defeated and miserable. French and English contemporary moralists viewed this fate as retribution for the murder of Becket;<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> even his favourite legitimate son, John, had rebelled although the constantly loyal illegitimate son Geoffrey remained with Henry until the end.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following Richard\'s coronation he quickly put the kingdom\'s affairs in order and departed on a Crusade for the Middle East. Opinion of Richard has fluctuated. Although he was respected for his military leadership and courtly manners, he had rejected and humiliated the sister of the king of France, deposed the king of Cyprus and later sold the island, he made enemies on the <a href="/wiki/Third_Crusade" title="Third Crusade">Third Crusade</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Leopold_V,_Duke_of_Austria" title="Leopold V, Duke of Austria">Leopold V, Duke of Austria</a> by showing disrespect to his banners as well as refusing to share the spoils of war, and was rumoured to have arranged the assassination of <a href="/wiki/Conrad_of_Montferrat" title="Conrad of Montferrat">Conrad of Montferrat</a>. His ruthlessness was demonstrated by his <a href="/wiki/Massacre_at_Ayyadieh" title="Massacre at Ayyadieh">massacre of 2,600 prisoners in Acre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He obtained victories during the Third Crusade, but failed to capture <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Steven_Runciman" title="Steven Runciman">Steven Runciman</a> Richard was "a bad son, a bad husband and a bad king".<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Riley-Smith" title="Jonathan Riley-Smith">Jonathan Riley-Smith</a> described him as "vain&#160;... devious and self-centred".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In an alternate view <a href="/wiki/John_Gillingham" title="John Gillingham">John Gillingham</a> points out that for centuries Richard was considered a model king.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Returning from the crusade with a small band of followers, Richard was captured by Leopold and was passed to <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Henry VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Henry VI</a>. Henry held Richard captive for eighteen months (1192&#8211;1194) while his mother raised the ransom, valued at 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Mark_(currency)#England_and_Scotland" title="Mark (currency)">marks</a>.  In Richard\'s absence, Philip II overran large portions of Normandy and John acquired control of Richard\'s English lands. After returning to England, Richard forgave John and re-established his authority in England. He left again in 1194 and battled Philip for five years, attempting to regain the lands seized during his captivity. When close to complete victory, he was injured by an arrow during a siege and died ten days later.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline_and_the_loss_of_Anjou">Decline and the loss of Anjou</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Decline and the loss of Anjou">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Magna_Carta_(British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of one of the four surviving copies of Magna Carta held in British Museum" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg/220px-Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg/330px-Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg/440px-Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7200" data-file-height="4800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Magna_Carta_(British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of only four surviving <a href="/wiki/Exemplified_copy" title="Exemplified copy">exemplifications</a> of the 1215 text of <a href="/wiki/Magna_Carta" title="Magna Carta">Magna Carta</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a>, London.</div></div></div>\n<p>Richard\'s failure to provide an heir caused a succession crisis and conflict between supporters of the claim of his nephew, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_I,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Arthur I, Duke of Brittany">Arthur</a>, and John. <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_des_Roches" class="mw-redirect" title="Guillaume des Roches">Guillaume des Roches</a> led the magnates of Anjou, Maine, and Touraine declaring for Arthur.<sup id="cite_ref-JohnONDB_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JohnONDB-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Once again Philip II of France attempted to disturb the Plantagenet territories on the European mainland by supporting his vassal Arthur\'s claim to the English crown. John won a significant victory while preventing Arthur\'s forces from capturing his mother, seizing the entire rebel leadership at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mirebeau" title="Battle of Mirebeau">Battle of Mirebeau</a> and his sister <a href="/wiki/Eleanor,_Fair_Maid_of_Brittany" title="Eleanor, Fair Maid of Brittany">Eleanor, Fair Maid of Brittany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>  Foolishly John disregarded his allies\' opinions on the fate of the prisoners, many of them their neighbours and kinsmen. Instead he kept his prisoners so vilely and in such evil distress that it seemed shameful and ugly to all those who were with him and who saw this cruelty\' according to the <a href="/wiki/L%27Histoire_de_Guillaume_le_Marechal" title="L&#39;Histoire de Guillaume le Marechal">L\'Histoire de Guillaume le Marechal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JohnONDB_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JohnONDB-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> As a result of John\'s behaviour the powerful Thouars, Lusignan, and des Roches families rebelled and John lost control of Anjou, Maine, Touraine, and northern Poitou. His son, King Henry III, maintained the claim to the Angevin territories until December 1259 when he formally surrendered them and in return was granted Gascony as duke of Aquitaine and a vassal of the king of France.<sup id="cite_ref-RidgewayH3ONDB_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RidgewayH3ONDB-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> John\'s reputation was further damaged by the rumour, described in the <a href="/wiki/Margam_Abbey" title="Margam Abbey">Margam annals</a>, that while drunk he himself had murdered Arthur and if not true it is almost certain John ordered the killing.<sup id="cite_ref-JohnONDB_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JohnONDB-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> There are two contrasting schools of thought explaining the sudden collapse of John\'s position. <a href="/wiki/J._C._Holt" title="J. C. Holt">Sir James Holt</a> suggests this was the inevitable result of superior French resources. <a href="/wiki/John_Gillingham" title="John Gillingham">John Gillingham</a> identifies diplomatic and military mismanagement and points out that Richard managed to hold the Angevin territory with comparable finances.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Nick Barratt has calculated that Angevin resources available for use in the war were 22 per cent less than those of Phillip, putting the Angevins at a disadvantage.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 1214 John had re-established his authority in England and planned what Gillingham has called a grand strategy to recapture Normandy and Anjou.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The plan was that John would draw the French from <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, while another army, under his nephew <a href="/wiki/Otto_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto IV</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>, and his half-brother William attacked from the north. He also brought his niece Eleanor of Brittany, aiming to establish her as Duchess of Brittany. The plan failed when John\'s allies were defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bouvines" title="Battle of Bouvines">Battle of Bouvines</a>. Otto retreated and was soon overthrown, William was captured by the French and John agreed to a five-year truce.<sup id="cite_ref-Longespee_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Longespee-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JohnONDB_43-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JohnONDB-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> (From then on John also gave up the claim to Brittany of Eleanor and had her confined for life.)<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> John\'s defeat weakened his authority in England, and his barons forced him to agree to the <a href="/wiki/Magna_Carta" title="Magna Carta">Magna Carta</a>, which limited royal power. Both sides failed to abide by the terms of the Magna Carta, leading to the <a href="/wiki/First_Barons%27_War" title="First Barons&#39; War">First Barons\' War</a>, in which rebellious barons invited <a href="/wiki/Louis_VIII_of_France" title="Louis VIII of France">Prince Louis</a>, the husband of <a href="/wiki/Blanche_of_Castile" title="Blanche of Castile">Blanche</a>, Henry II\'s granddaughter, to invade England.<sup id="cite_ref-JohnONDB_43-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JohnONDB-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>  Louis did so but in October 1216, before the conflict was conclusively ended,  John died.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The official website of the British Monarchy presents John\'s death as the end of the Angevin dynasty and the beginning of the Plantagenet dynasty.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_line">Main line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Main line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baronial_conflict_and_the_establishment_of_Parliament">Baronial conflict and the establishment of Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Baronial conflict and the establishment of Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>All subsequent English monarchs were descendants of the Angevin line via John, who had five legitimate children with <a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Angoul%C3%AAme" title="Isabella of Angoul\xc3\xaame">Isabella</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_England" title="Henry III of England">Henry III</a> \xe2\x80\x93 king of England for most of the 13th-century</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Richard,_1st_Earl_of_Cornwall" title="Richard, 1st Earl of Cornwall">Richard</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romans" title="King of the Romans">king of the Romans</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joan_of_England,_Queen_consort_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Joan of England, Queen consort of Scotland">Joan</a> \xe2\x80\x93 queen consort of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Scotland" title="Alexander II of Scotland">Alexander II of Scotland</a><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_England" title="Isabella of England">Isabella</a> \xe2\x80\x93 wife of the Holy Roman Emperor, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick II</a><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Leicester" class="mw-redirect" title="Eleanor of Leicester">Eleanor</a> \xe2\x80\x93 wife of <a href="/wiki/William_Marshal,_1st_Earl_of_Pembroke" title="William Marshal, 1st Earl of Pembroke">William Marshal</a>\'s son (also named <a href="/wiki/William_Marshal,_2nd_Earl_of_Pembroke" title="William Marshal, 2nd Earl of Pembroke">William</a>), and later the English rebel <a href="/wiki/Simon_de_Montfort,_6th_Earl_of_Leicester" title="Simon de Montfort, 6th Earl of Leicester">Simon de Montfort</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>John also had illegitimate children with several mistresses. These children probably included nine sons called <a href="/wiki/Richard_FitzRoy" title="Richard FitzRoy">Richard</a>, Oliver, Henry, Osbert Gifford, Geoffrey, John FitzJohn or Courcy, Odo or Eudes FitzRoy, Ivo, Henry, Richard the constable of <a href="/wiki/Wallingford_Castle" title="Wallingford Castle">Wallingford Castle</a> and three daughters called <a href="/wiki/Joan,_Lady_of_Wales" title="Joan, Lady of Wales">Joan</a>, Matilda the abbess of Barking and Isabella la Blanche.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Joan was the best known of these, since she married Prince <a href="/wiki/Llewelyn_the_Great" class="mw-redirect" title="Llewelyn the Great">Llewelyn the Great</a> of Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WLA_vanda_Cast_of_Tomb_Effigy_Henry_III.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of the Cast of the effigy of King Henry the third in Westminster Abbey, c. 1272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/WLA_vanda_Cast_of_Tomb_Effigy_Henry_III.jpg/220px-WLA_vanda_Cast_of_Tomb_Effigy_Henry_III.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/WLA_vanda_Cast_of_Tomb_Effigy_Henry_III.jpg/330px-WLA_vanda_Cast_of_Tomb_Effigy_Henry_III.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/WLA_vanda_Cast_of_Tomb_Effigy_Henry_III.jpg/440px-WLA_vanda_Cast_of_Tomb_Effigy_Henry_III.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4147" data-file-height="2674" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WLA_vanda_Cast_of_Tomb_Effigy_Henry_III.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cast of the <a href="/wiki/Tomb_effigy" title="Tomb effigy">tomb effigy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_England" title="Henry III of England">Henry III</a> in <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>, c.1272.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/William_Marshal,_1st_Earl_of_Pembroke" title="William Marshal, 1st Earl of Pembroke">William Marshal, 1st Earl of Pembroke</a>, was appointed regent for the nine-year-old King Henry on King John\'s death. Thereafter, support for Louis declined, and he renounced his claims in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lambeth" title="Treaty of Lambeth">Treaty of Lambeth</a> after Marshal\'s victories at the battles of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lincoln_(1217)" title="Battle of Lincoln (1217)">Lincoln</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sandwich_(1217)" title="Battle of Sandwich (1217)">Sandwich</a> in 1217.<sup id="cite_ref-RidgewayH3ONDB_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RidgewayH3ONDB-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>  The Marshal regime issued an amended Magna Carta as a basis for future government.<sup id="cite_ref-RidgewayH3ONDB_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RidgewayH3ONDB-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Despite the Treaty of Lambeth, hostilities continued and Henry was forced to compromise with the newly crowned Louis VIII of France and Henry\'s stepfather, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_X_of_Lusignan" title="Hugh X of Lusignan">Hugh X of Lusignan</a>. They both overran much of Henry\'s remaining continental lands, further eroding the Angevins\' power on the continent. In his political struggles, Henry perceived many similarities between himself and England\'s patron saint, <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Confessor" title="Edward the Confessor">Edward the Confessor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, he named his first son Edward and built the existing magnificent shrine for the Confessor.<sup id="cite_ref-Schama2000p172_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schama2000p172-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In early 1225 a great council approved a tax of \xc2\xa340,000 to dispatch an army, which quickly retook Gascony. During an assembly feudal prerogatives of the king were challenged by the barons, bishops and magnates who demanded that the king reissue the <i>Magna Carta</i> and the Charter of the Forest in exchange for support.  Henry declared that the charters were issued of his own "spontaneous and free will" and confirmed them with the royal seal, giving the new <a href="/wiki/Magna_Carta#The_Great_Charter_1225" title="Magna Carta">Great Charter</a> and the Charter of the Forest of 1225 much more authority than any previous versions.<sup id="cite_ref-RidgewayH3ONDB_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RidgewayH3ONDB-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Henry III had nine children:<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Edward_I_of_England" title="Edward I of England">Edward I</a> (1239\xe2\x80\x931307)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_England" title="Margaret of England">Margaret of England</a> (1240\xe2\x80\x931275). Her three children predeceased her husband, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Scotland" title="Alexander III of Scotland">Alexander III of Scotland</a>; consequently, the crown of Scotland became vacant on the death of their only grandchild, <a href="/wiki/Margaret,_Maid_of_Norway" title="Margaret, Maid of Norway">Margaret, Maid of Norway</a> in 1290.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Beatrice_of_England" title="Beatrice of England">Beatrice, Countess of Richmond</a> (1242\xe2\x80\x931275). She initially married John de Montfort of Dreux, and later married <a href="/wiki/John_II,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="John II, Duke of Brittany">John II, Duke of Brittany</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edmund_Crouchback" title="Edmund Crouchback">Edmund Crouchback</a> (1245\xe2\x80\x931296), who was granted the titles and estates of <a href="/wiki/Simon_de_Montfort,_6th_Earl_of_Leicester" title="Simon de Montfort, 6th Earl of Leicester">Simon de Montfort, 6th Earl of Leicester</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Leicester" title="Earl of Leicester">earldom of Leicester</a> after Henry defeated Montfort in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Barons%27_War" title="Second Barons&#39; War">Second Barons\' War</a>. Henry later granted Edmund the earldoms of <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Lancaster" title="Earl of Lancaster">Lancaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Earl_Ferrers" title="Earl Ferrers">Ferrers</a>. From 1276, through his wife, Edmund was <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Champagne" title="Count of Champagne">Count of Champagne</a> and Brie.<sup id="cite_ref-Weir2008_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weir2008-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Later Lancastrians would attempt to use Henry IV\'s maternal descent from Edmund to legitimise his claim to the throne, spuriously claiming that Edmund was the eldest son of Henry III but had not become king due to deformity.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Through his second marriage to <a href="/wiki/Blanche_of_Artois" title="Blanche of Artois">Blanche</a>, the widow of <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_Navarre" title="Henry I of Navarre">Henry I of Navarre</a>, Edmund was at the centre of European aristocracy. Blanche\'s daughter, <a href="/wiki/Joan_I_of_Navarre" title="Joan I of Navarre">Joan</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Queen_regnant" title="Queen regnant">queen regnant</a> of Navarre and queen consort of France through her marriage to <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_France" title="Philip IV of France">Philip IV</a>. Edmund\'s son <a href="/wiki/Thomas,_2nd_Earl_of_Lancaster" title="Thomas, 2nd Earl of Lancaster">Thomas</a> became the most powerful nobleman in England, adding to his inheritance the earldoms of <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Lincoln" title="Earl of Lincoln">Lincoln</a> and <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Salisbury" title="Earl of Salisbury">Salisbury</a> through his marriage to the heiress of <a href="/wiki/Henry_de_Lacy,_3rd_Earl_of_Lincoln" title="Henry de Lacy, 3rd Earl of Lincoln">Henry de Lacy, 3rd Earl of Lincoln</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TEoLONDB_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TEoLONDB-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Four others who died as children: Richard (1247\xe2\x80\x931256), John (1250\xe2\x80\x931256), William (c. 1251/1252\xe2\x80\x931256), <a href="/wiki/Katherine_of_England" title="Katherine of England">Katherine</a> (c. 1252/3\xe2\x80\x931257) and Henry (no recorded dates).</li></ul><p>\nHenry was bankrupted by his military expenditure and general extravagance. The pope offered Henry\'s brother <a href="/wiki/Richard,_1st_Earl_of_Cornwall" title="Richard, 1st Earl of Cornwall">Richard</a> the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a>, but the military cost of displacing the incumbent <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Frederick</a> was prohibitive. <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Paris" title="Matthew Paris">Matthew Paris</a> wrote that Richard stated: "You might as well say, \'I make you a present of the moon\xe2\x80\x94step up to the sky and take it down\'." Instead, Henry purchased the kingdom for his son Edmund, which angered many powerful barons. The barons led by Henry\'s brother-in-law Simon de Montfort forced him to agree to the <a href="/wiki/Provisions_of_Oxford" title="Provisions of Oxford">Provisions of Oxford</a>, under which his debts were paid in exchange for substantial reforms. In France, with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1259)" title="Treaty of Paris (1259)">Treaty of Paris</a>, Henry formally surrendered the territory of his Angevin ancestors to <a href="/wiki/Louis_IX_of_France" title="Louis IX of France">Louis IX of France</a>, receiving in return the title duke of Aquitaine and the territory of Gascony as a vassal of the French king.<sup id="cite_ref-RidgewayH3ONDB_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RidgewayH3ONDB-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montfort_Evesham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of a 13th-century representation of the death of Simon de Montfort" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Montfort_Evesham.jpg/220px-Montfort_Evesham.jpg" width="220" height="65" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Montfort_Evesham.jpg/330px-Montfort_Evesham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Montfort_Evesham.jpg/440px-Montfort_Evesham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="147" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montfort_Evesham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Death of Simon de Montfort at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Evesham" title="Battle of Evesham">Battle of Evesham</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Disagreements between the barons and the king intensified. The barons, under <a href="/wiki/Simon_de_Montfort,_6th_Earl_of_Leicester" title="Simon de Montfort, 6th Earl of Leicester">Simon de Montfort, 6th Earl of Leicester</a>, captured most of southeast England in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Barons%27_War" title="Second Barons&#39; War">Second Barons\' War</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lewes" title="Battle of Lewes">Battle of Lewes</a> in 1264, Henry and Prince Edward were defeated and taken prisoner. De Montfort assembled the <a href="/wiki/Montfort%27s_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Montfort&#39;s Parliament">Great Parliament</a>, recognized as the first Parliament because it was the first time the cities and boroughs had sent representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-Schama2000p181_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schama2000p181-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Edward escaped, raised an army and defeated and killed de Montfort at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Evesham" title="Battle of Evesham">Battle of Evesham</a> in 1265.<sup id="cite_ref-EIODNB_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIODNB-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Savage retribution was inflicted upon the rebels, and authority restored to Henry. With the realm now peaceful, Edward left England to join Louis IX on the <a href="/wiki/Ninth_Crusade" title="Ninth Crusade">Ninth Crusade</a>; he was one of the last crusaders. Louis died before Edward\'s arrival, but Edward decided to continue. The result was disappointing; Edward\'s small force only enabled him to capture <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a> and launch a handful of raids. After surviving an assassination attempt, Edward left for Sicily later in the year, never to participate in a crusade again. When Henry III died, Edward acceded to the throne; the barons swore allegiance to him even though he did not return for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-EIODNB_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIODNB-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_change_and_the_reform_of_feudalism">Constitutional change and the reform of feudalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Constitutional change and the reform of feudalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Edward I married <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Castile" title="Eleanor of Castile">Eleanor of Castile</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_III_of_Castile" title="Ferdinand III of Castile">King Ferdinand of Castile</a>, a great grandson of Henry II through his second daughter Eleanor in 1254. Edward and Eleanor had sixteen children; five daughters survived to adulthood, but only one son survived Edward:<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_England,_Countess_of_Bar" title="Eleanor of England, Countess of Bar">Eleanor, Countess of Bar</a> (1264/69\xe2\x88\x921298)</li>\n<li>Three daughters (Joan, Alice, and Juliana/Katherine) and two sons (John and Henry) born between 1265 and 1271. They died between 1265 and 1274 with little historical trace.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joan_of_Acre" title="Joan of Acre">Joan, Countess of Gloucester</a> (1272\xe2\x80\x931307)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alphonso,_Earl_of_Chester" title="Alphonso, Earl of Chester">Alphonso, Earl of Chester</a> (1273\xe2\x80\x931284)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_England,_Duchess_of_Brabant" title="Margaret of England, Duchess of Brabant">Margaret, Duchess of Brabant</a> (1275\xe2\x80\x931333)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Woodstock" title="Mary of Woodstock">Mary of Woodstock</a> (1278\xe2\x80\x931332), who became a <a href="/wiki/Nun" title="Nun">nun</a></li>\n<li>Isabella (1279\xe2\x80\x931279)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Rhuddlan" title="Elizabeth of Rhuddlan">Elizabeth, firstly Countess of Holland and on widowhood, secondly Countess of Hereford</a> (1282\xe2\x80\x931316). Among her eleven children were the earls of <a href="/wiki/Hereford" title="Hereford">Hereford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northampton" title="Northampton">Northampton</a>, and the countesses of <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Ormond_(Scotland)" title="Earl of Ormond (Scotland)">Ormond</a> and <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edward_II_of_England" title="Edward II of England">Edward II</a></li>\n<li>Two other daughters (Beatrice and Blanche), who died as children.</li></ul>\n<p>Following Eleanor\'s death in 1290, Edward married <a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_France,_Queen_of_England" title="Margaret of France, Queen of England">Margaret of France</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Philip_III_of_France" title="Philip III of France">Philip III of France</a>, in 1299. Edward and Margaret had two sons, who both lived to adulthood, and a daughter who died as a child:<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_of_Brotherton,_1st_Earl_of_Norfolk" title="Thomas of Brotherton, 1st Earl of Norfolk">Thomas</a> (1300\xe2\x80\x931338), whose daughter <a href="/wiki/Margaret,_Duchess_of_Norfolk" title="Margaret, Duchess of Norfolk">Margaret</a> inherited his estates. Margaret\'s grandson, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_de_Mowbray,_1st_Duke_of_Norfolk" title="Thomas de Mowbray, 1st Duke of Norfolk">Thomas Mowbray</a>, was the first <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Norfolk" title="Duke of Norfolk">duke of Norfolk</a>, but Richard II exiled him and stripped him of his titles.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edmund_of_Woodstock,_1st_Earl_of_Kent" title="Edmund of Woodstock, 1st Earl of Kent">Edmund, Earl of Kent</a> (1301 to 1330). Edmund\'s loyalty to his half-brother, Edward II, resulted in his execution by order of the rebel Mortimer and his lover, Edward\'s queen, Isabella. His daughter, Joan, inherited his estates and married her own cousin, <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Black_Prince" title="Edward the Black Prince">Edward the Black Prince</a>; together, they had <a href="/wiki/Richard_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard II">Richard</a>, who later became the English king.</li>\n<li>Eleanor (1306\xe2\x80\x931311).</li></ul>\n<p>Evidence for Edward\'s involvement in legal reform is hard to find but his reign saw a major programme of legal change. Much of the drive and determination is likely to have come from the king and his experience of the baronial reform movement of the late 1250s and early 1260s. With the <a href="/wiki/Statutes_of_Mortmain" title="Statutes of Mortmain">Statutes of Mortmain</a>, Edward imposed his authority over the Church; the statutes prohibited land donation to the Church, asserted the rights of the Crown at the expense of traditional feudal privileges, promoted the uniform administration of justice, raised income and codified the legal system. His military campaigns left him in heavy debt and when <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_France" title="Philip IV of France">Philip IV of France</a> confiscated the Duchy of <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Gascony</a> in 1294, Edward needed funds to wage war in France. When Edward summoned a precedent-setting <a href="/wiki/Model_Parliament" title="Model Parliament">assembly</a> in order to raise more taxes for military finance, he included lesser landowners and merchants. The resulting parliament included barons, clergy, knights, and burgesses for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-EIODNB_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIODNB-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_in_Britain">Expansion in Britain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Expansion in Britain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_Scottish_Independence" title="Wars of Scottish Independence">Wars of Scottish Independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Wales_by_Edward_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Conquest of Wales by Edward I">Conquest of Wales by Edward I</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_after_the_Treaty_of_Montgomery_1267.svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of Wales in 1267 showing territory controlled by Edward and various Welsh princes" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Wales_after_the_Treaty_of_Montgomery_1267.svg/170px-Wales_after_the_Treaty_of_Montgomery_1267.svg.png" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Wales_after_the_Treaty_of_Montgomery_1267.svg/255px-Wales_after_the_Treaty_of_Montgomery_1267.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Wales_after_the_Treaty_of_Montgomery_1267.svg/340px-Wales_after_the_Treaty_of_Montgomery_1267.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="1052" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_after_the_Treaty_of_Montgomery_1267.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wales after the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Montgomery" title="Treaty of Montgomery">Treaty of Montgomery</a> in 1267 <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #87de87; color:black;
