font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Gwynedd" class="mw-redirect" title="Principality of Gwynedd">Gwynedd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Llywelyn_ap_Gruffudd" title="Llywelyn ap Gruffudd">Llywelyn ap Gruffudd</a>\'s principality</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ddafe9; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Territories conquered by Llywelyn</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #aaeeff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Territories of Llywelyn\'s vassals</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffb380; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Lordships of the <a href="/wiki/Marcher_barons" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcher barons">Marcher barons</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #eeffaa; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Lordships of the king of England</div></div></div></div>\n<p>On his accession, Edward I sought to organise his realm, enforcing his claims to primacy in the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>. <a href="/wiki/Llywelyn_ap_Gruffudd" title="Llywelyn ap Gruffudd">Llywelyn ap Gruffudd</a> claimed to rule <a href="/wiki/North_Wales" title="North Wales">North Wales</a> "entirely separate from" England but Edward viewed him to be "a rebel and disturber of the peace". Edward\'s determination, military experience and skilful naval manoeuvres ended what was to him rebellion. The invasion was executed by one of the largest armies ever assembled by an English king, comprising Anglo-Norman cavalry and Welsh archers and laying the foundation for future victories in France. Llywelyn was driven into the mountains, later dying in battle. The <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Rhuddlan" title="Statute of Rhuddlan">Statute of Rhuddlan</a> established England\'s authority over Wales, and Edward\'s son was proclaimed the first English <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a> upon his birth. Edward spent vast sums on his two Welsh campaigns with a large portion of it spent on a network of castles.<sup id="cite_ref-EIODNB_67-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIODNB-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Edward asserted that the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Scottish_monarchs" title="List of Scottish monarchs">king of Scotland</a> owed him feudal allegiance, and intended to unite the two nations by marrying his son <a href="/wiki/Edward_II_of_England" title="Edward II of England">Edward</a> to <a href="/wiki/Margaret,_Maid_of_Norway" title="Margaret, Maid of Norway">Margaret</a>, the sole heir of King <a href="/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Scotland" title="Alexander III of Scotland">Alexander III</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EIODNB_67-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIODNB-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> When Margaret died in 1290, <a href="/wiki/Competitors_for_the_Crown_of_Scotland" title="Competitors for the Crown of Scotland">competition for the Scottish crown</a> ensued. By invitation of Scottish magnates, Edward I resolved the dispute, ruling in favour of <a href="/wiki/John_Balliol" title="John Balliol">John Balliol</a>, who duly swore loyalty to him and became king. Edward insisted that he was Scotland\'s sovereign and possessed the right to hear appeals against Balliol\'s judgements, undermining Balliol\'s authority. Balliol allied with France in 1295; Edward invaded Scotland the following year, deposing and exiling Balliol.<sup id="cite_ref-EIODNB_67-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIODNB-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nEdward was less successful in Gascony, which was overrun by the French. With his resources depleting, Edward was forced to reconfirm the Charters, including Magna Carta, to obtain the necessary funds. In 1303 the French king restored Gascony to Edward by signing the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1303)" title="Treaty of Paris (1303)">Treaty of Paris</a>. Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/William_Wallace" title="William Wallace">William Wallace</a> rose in Balliol\'s name and recovered most of Scotland. Wallace was defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Falkirk_(1298)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Falkirk (1298)">Battle of Falkirk</a>, after which <a href="/wiki/Robert_the_Bruce" title="Robert the Bruce">Robert the Bruce</a> rebelled and was crowned king of Scotland. Edward died while travelling to Scotland for another campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-EIODNB_67-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIODNB-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_from_Holkham_Bible.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Image of the Battle of Bannockburn reproduced from the Holkham Bible" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Battle_from_Holkham_Bible.jpg/170px-Battle_from_Holkham_Bible.jpg" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Battle_from_Holkham_Bible.jpg/255px-Battle_from_Holkham_Bible.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Battle_from_Holkham_Bible.jpg/340px-Battle_from_Holkham_Bible.jpg 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_from_Holkham_Bible.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scene from the <a href="/wiki/Holkham_Bible" title="Holkham Bible">Holkham Bible</a> showing knights and foot soldiers from the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bannockburn" title="Battle of Bannockburn">Battle of Bannockburn</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>King Edward II\'s coronation oath on his succession in 1307 was the first to reflect the king\'s responsibility to maintain the laws that the community "shall have chosen" (<i lang="frm" title="Middle French language text">aura eslu</i> in French).<sup id="cite_ref-McKisack19594_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKisack19594-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> He was not unpopular initially but faced three challenges: discontent over the financing of wars; his household spending; and the role of his <a href="/wiki/Favourite" title="Favourite">favourite</a> <a href="/wiki/Piers_Gaveston" class="mw-redirect" title="Piers Gaveston">Piers Gaveston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIODNB_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIODNB-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> When Parliament decided that Gaveston should be exiled the king was left with no choice but to comply.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBPG_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBPG-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Edward engineered Gaveston\'s return, but was forced to agree to the appointment of <a href="/wiki/Ordainers" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordainers">Ordainers</a>, led by his cousin <a href="/wiki/Thomas,_2nd_Earl_of_Lancaster" title="Thomas, 2nd Earl of Lancaster">Thomas, 2nd Earl of Lancaster</a>, to reform the royal household with Piers Gaveston exiled again.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIODNB_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIODNB-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> When Gaveston returned again to England, he was abducted and executed after a mock trial.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBPG_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBPG-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The ramifications of this drove Thomas and his adherents from power. Edward\'s humiliating defeat by Bruce at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bannockburn" title="Battle of Bannockburn">Battle of Bannockburn</a>, confirming Bruce\'s position as an independent king of Scots, leading to Lancaster being appointed head of the king\'s council.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIODNB_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIODNB-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Edward finally repealed the Ordinances after defeating and executing Lancaster at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Boroughbridge" title="Battle of Boroughbridge">Battle of Boroughbridge</a> in 1322.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIODNB_71-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIODNB-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The French monarchy asserted its rights to encroach on Edward\'s legal rights in Gascony. Resistance to one judgement in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Sardos,_Lot-et-Garonne" title="Saint-Sardos, Lot-et-Garonne">Saint-Sardos</a> resulted in Charles IV declaring the duchy forfeit. Charles\'s sister, <a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_France" title="Isabella of France">Queen Isabella</a>, was sent to negotiate and agreed a treaty that required Edward to pay homage in France to Charles. Edward resigned Aquitaine and Ponthieu to his son <a href="/wiki/Edward_III_of_England" title="Edward III of England">Edward</a>, who travelled to France to give homage in his stead. With the English heir in her power, Isabella refused to return to England unless Edward II dismissed his favourites, and she became the mistress of <a href="/wiki/Roger_Mortimer,_1st_Earl_of_March" title="Roger Mortimer, 1st Earl of March">Roger Mortimer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIODNB_71-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIODNB-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The couple invaded England and, with <a href="/wiki/Henry,_3rd_Earl_of_Lancaster" title="Henry, 3rd Earl of Lancaster">Henry, 3rd Earl of Lancaster</a>, captured the king.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBToL_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBToL-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Edward II abdicated on condition that his son would inherit the throne rather than Mortimer. Although there is no historical record of the cause of death, he is popularly believed to have been murdered at Berkeley Castle by having a red-hot poker thrust into his bowels.<sup id="cite_ref-Schama220_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schama220-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EIIIdeath_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIIdeath-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> A coup by Edward III ended four years of control by Isabella and Mortimer. Mortimer was executed. Though removed from power, Isabella was treated well, and lived in luxury for the next 27 years.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIODNB_71-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIODNB-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict_with_the_House_of_Valois">Conflict with the House of Valois</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Conflict with the House of Valois">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years&#39; War">Hundred Years\' War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War_(1337%E2%80%9360)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred Years&#39; War (1337\xe2\x80\x9360)">Hundred Years\' War (1337\xe2\x80\x9360)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War_(1369%E2%80%9389)" title="Hundred Years&#39; War (1369\xe2\x80\x9389)">Hundred Years\' War (1369\xe2\x80\x9389)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Philip_iv_and_family.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Image of vellum manuscript from 1313 of Isabella, third from left, with her father, Philip IV, her future French king brothers, and Philip&#39;s brother, Charles of Valois" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Philip_iv_and_family.jpg/220px-Philip_iv_and_family.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Philip_iv_and_family.jpg/330px-Philip_iv_and_family.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Philip_iv_and_family.jpg/440px-Philip_iv_and_family.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="395" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Philip_iv_and_family.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_France" title="Isabella of France">Isabella</a> (third from left) with her father, <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_France" title="Philip IV of France">Philip IV</a>, her future French king brothers, and Philip\'s brother, <a href="/wiki/Charles_of_Valois" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles of Valois">Charles of Valois</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1328 <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_France" title="Charles IV of France">Charles IV of France</a> died without a male heir. Queen Isabella made a claim to throne of France on behalf of her son Edward on the grounds that he was a <a href="/wiki/Matrilineal" class="mw-redirect" title="Matrilineal">matrilineal</a> grandson of Philip IV of France. However, the precedents set by Philip V\'s succession over his niece <a href="/wiki/Joan_II_of_Navarre" title="Joan II of Navarre">Joan II of Navarre</a> and Charles IV\'s succession over his nieces meant that the senior grandson of Philip III in the male line, Phillip of Valois, became king. Not yet in power, Edward paid homage to Phillip as Duke of Aquitaine.\n</p><p>In 1337 Phillip confiscated Aquitaine and Ponthieu from Edward alleging he was harbouring Phillip\xe2\x80\x99s fugitive cousin and enemy, <a href="/wiki/Robert_III_of_Artois" title="Robert III of Artois">Robert of Artois</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIIODNB_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIIODNB-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In response, Edward proclaimed himself king of France to encourage the Flemish to rise in open rebellion against the French king. The conflict, later known as the Hundred Years\' War, included a significant English naval victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sluys" title="Battle of Sluys">Battle of Sluys</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EIIIODNB_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIIODNB-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and a victory on land at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cr%C3%A9cy" title="Battle of Cr\xc3\xa9cy">Cr\xc3\xa9cy</a>, leaving Edward free to capture the important port of <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a>. A subsequent victory against Scotland at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Neville%27s_Cross" title="Battle of Neville&#39;s Cross">Battle of Neville\'s Cross</a> resulted in the capture of <a href="/wiki/David_II_of_Scotland" title="David II of Scotland">David II</a> and reduced the threat from Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIIODNB_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIIODNB-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Black_Death_in_England" title="Black Death in England">Black Death</a> brought a halt to Edward\'s campaigns by killing perhaps a third of his subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIIODNB_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIIODNB-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The only Plantagenet known to have died from the Black Death was Edward III\'s daughter <a href="/wiki/Joan_of_England_(1335%E2%80%931348)" title="Joan of England (1335\xe2\x80\x931348)">Joan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIIODNB_76-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIIODNB-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_crecy_froissart.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Image of the Battle of Crecy taken from Froissart" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Battle_of_crecy_froissart.jpg/220px-Battle_of_crecy_froissart.jpg" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Battle_of_crecy_froissart.jpg/330px-Battle_of_crecy_froissart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Battle_of_crecy_froissart.jpg/440px-Battle_of_crecy_froissart.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1998" data-file-height="1755" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_crecy_froissart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cr%C3%A9cy" title="Battle of Cr\xc3\xa9cy">Battle of Cr\xc3\xa9cy</a> was an important Plantagenet victory of the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years&#39; War">Hundred Years\' War</a> in France. <a href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_nationale_de_France" title="Biblioth\xc3\xa8que nationale de France">Biblioth\xc3\xa8que nationale de France</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Edward,_the_Black_Prince" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward, the Black Prince">Edward, the Black Prince</a> resumed the war with destructive <a href="/wiki/Chevauch%C3%A9e" title="Chevauch\xc3\xa9e">chevauch\xc3\xa9es</a> starting from Bordeaux. His army was caught by a much larger French force at <a href="/wiki/Poitiers" title="Poitiers">Poitiers</a>, but the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Poitiers" title="Battle of Poitiers">battle</a> was a decisive English victory resulting in the capture of <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_France" title="John II of France">John II of France</a>. John agreed a <a href="/wiki/Second_Treaty_of_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Treaty of London">treaty</a> promising the French would pay a four million \xc3\xa9cus ransom. The subsequent <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Br%C3%A9tigny" title="Treaty of Br\xc3\xa9tigny">Treaty of Br\xc3\xa9tigny</a> was demonstrably popular in England, where it was both ratified in parliament and celebrated with great ceremony. To reach agreement, clauses were removed that would have had Edward renounce his claim to the French crown in return for territory in Aquitaine and the town of Calais. These were entered in another agreement to be effected only after the transfer of territory by November 1361 but both sides prevaricated over their commitments for the following nine years. Hostages from the Valois family were held in London while John returned to France to raise his ransom. Edward had restored the lands of the former Angevin Empire holding Normandy, Brittany, Anjou, Maine and the coastline from <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a> to Spain. When the hostages escaped back to France, John was horrified that his word had been broken and returned to England, where he eventually died.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIIODNB_76-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIIODNB-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fighting in the Hundred Years\' War spilled from the French and Plantagenet lands into surrounding realms, including the dynastic conflict in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Castile</a> between Peter of Castile and <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_Castile" title="Henry II of Castile">Henry II of Castile</a>. The Black Prince allied himself with Peter, defeating Henry at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%C3%A1jera" title="Battle of N\xc3\xa1jera">Battle of N\xc3\xa1jera</a>. Edward and Peter fell out when Peter was unable to reimburse Edward\xe2\x80\x99s military expenses leaving him bankrupt.<sup id="cite_ref-Black_Prince_ODNB_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Prince_ODNB-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The Plantagenets continued to interfere, and <a href="/wiki/John_of_Gaunt,_1st_Duke_of_Lancaster" class="mw-redirect" title="John of Gaunt, 1st Duke of Lancaster">John of Gaunt, 1st Duke of Lancaster</a>, the Black Prince\'s brother, married Peter\'s daughter <a href="/wiki/Constance_of_Castile,_Duchess_of_Lancaster" title="Constance of Castile, Duchess of Lancaster">Constance</a>, claiming the Crown of Castile in her name. He invaded with an army of 5000 men. Fighting was inconclusive before Gaunt agreed a treaty with <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Castile" title="John I of Castile">King Juan of Castile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNGJoG_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNGJoG-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Terms of the treaty included the marriage of John of Gaunt\'s daughter <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Lancaster" title="Catherine of Lancaster">Katherine</a> to Juan\'s son, <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_Castile" title="Henry III of Castile">Enrique</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KoL_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KoL-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Charles_V_of_France" title="Charles V of France">Charles V of France</a> maintained the terms of the treaty of Br\xc3\xa9tigny but encouraged others in Aquitaine to challenge the authority of the Plantagenets in Aquitaine.<sup id="cite_ref-Black_Prince_ODNB_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Prince_ODNB-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The prince, who had suffered a debilitating illness for nearly a decade which often restricted his movement to being carried in a litter,<sup id="cite_ref-Black_Prince_ODNB_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Prince_ODNB-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> returned to England, where he soon died.<sup id="cite_ref-Weir2008p93_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weir2008p93-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> John of Gaunt assumed leadership in France with limited success, and peace negotiations over several years were inconclusive.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNGJoG_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNGJoG-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Descendants_of_Edward_III">Descendants of Edward III</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Descendants of Edward III">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean_Froissart,_Chroniques,_154v,_12148_btv1b8438605hf336,_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Image of Richard II and the peasants revolt taken from Froissart" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jean_Froissart%2C_Chroniques%2C_154v%2C_12148_btv1b8438605hf336%2C_crop.jpg/220px-Jean_Froissart%2C_Chroniques%2C_154v%2C_12148_btv1b8438605hf336%2C_crop.jpg"
