srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jean_Froissart%2C_Chroniques%2C_154v%2C_12148_btv1b8438605hf336%2C_crop.jpg/330px-Jean_Froissart%2C_Chroniques%2C_154v%2C_12148_btv1b8438605hf336%2C_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jean_Froissart%2C_Chroniques%2C_154v%2C_12148_btv1b8438605hf336%2C_crop.jpg/440px-Jean_Froissart%2C_Chroniques%2C_154v%2C_12148_btv1b8438605hf336%2C_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3261" data-file-height="3144" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean_Froissart,_Chroniques,_154v,_12148_btv1b8438605hf336,_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Richard_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard II">Richard II</a> meets the rebels of the <a href="/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt" title="Peasants&#39; Revolt">Peasants\' Revolt</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Illuminated_manuscript" title="Illuminated manuscript">illumination</a> from Froissart\'s <i>Chronicles</i>. <a href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_nationale_de_France" title="Biblioth\xc3\xa8que nationale de France">Biblioth\xc3\xa8que nationale de France</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The marriage of Edward III and <a href="/wiki/Philippa_of_Hainault" title="Philippa of Hainault">Philippa of Hainault</a> produced thirteen children and thirty-two grandchildren:<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Edward,_the_Black_Prince" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward, the Black Prince">Edward</a> (1330\xe2\x80\x931376)\xe2\x80\x94married his cousin <a href="/wiki/Joan_of_Kent" title="Joan of Kent">Joan of Kent</a>, a granddaughter of Edward I, with whom he had two sons:</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><ul><li>Edward (1365\xe2\x80\x931371/2)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_II_of_England" title="Richard II of England">Richard</a> (1367\xe2\x80\x931400)</li></ul></dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_England,_Lady_of_Coucy" class="mw-redirect" title="Isabella of England, Lady of Coucy">Isabella</a> (1332\xe2\x80\x931382)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Enguerrand_II,_Lord_of_Coucy" title="Enguerrand II, Lord of Coucy">Enguerrand II, Lord of Coucy</a>, and had two daughters:</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Marie_I_de_Coucy,_Countess_of_Soissons" title="Marie I de Coucy, Countess of Soissons">Marie</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Philippa_de_Coucy,_Countess_of_Oxford" title="Philippa de Coucy, Countess of Oxford">Philippa</a></li></ul></dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Joan_of_England_(1335%E2%80%931348)" title="Joan of England (1335\xe2\x80\x931348)">Joan</a> (1335\xe2\x80\x931348)</li>\n<li>William (1334/6\xe2\x80\x931337)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lionel_of_Antwerp,_1st_Duke_of_Clarence" title="Lionel of Antwerp, 1st Duke of Clarence">Lionel</a> (1338\xe2\x80\x931368)\xe2\x80\x94had one daughter with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_de_Burgh,_4th_Countess_of_Ulster" title="Elizabeth de Burgh, 4th Countess of Ulster">Elizabeth de Burgh</a>:</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Philippa,_5th_Countess_of_Ulster" title="Philippa, 5th Countess of Ulster">Philippa</a> (1355\xe2\x80\x931378/81)\xe2\x80\x94through Philippa, the House of York, by <a href="/wiki/Cognatic_kinship" title="Cognatic kinship">cognatic kinship</a>, asserted that its claim to the throne was superior to the House of Lancaster\'s. Philippa\'s granddaughter and heir, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Mortimer" class="mw-redirect" title="Anne Mortimer">Anne Mortimer</a>, married <a href="/wiki/Richard_of_Conisburgh,_3rd_Earl_of_Cambridge" title="Richard of Conisburgh, 3rd Earl of Cambridge">Richard of Conisburgh, 3rd Earl of Cambridge</a>, the Duke of York\'s heir. The <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Northumberland" title="Earl of Northumberland">earls of Northumberland</a> and Clifford, significant supporters of the Lancasters during the Wars of the Roses, were descendants of Philippa through her other daughter, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Mortimer" title="Elizabeth Mortimer">Elizabeth Mortimer</a>.</li></ul></dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_of_Gaunt" title="John of Gaunt">John of Gaunt</a> (1340\xe2\x80\x931399)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Blanche_of_Lancaster" title="Blanche of Lancaster">Blanche of Lancaster</a>, the heiress to the duchy of Lancaster and a direct descendant of Henry III, and had six children with her:</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Philippa_of_Lancaster" title="Philippa of Lancaster">Philippa</a> (1360\xe2\x80\x931415)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Portugal" title="John I of Portugal">John I of Portugal</a>.</li>\n<li>John (c. 1362/1364)\xe2\x80\x94died as an infant.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Lancaster,_Duchess_of_Exeter" title="Elizabeth of Lancaster, Duchess of Exeter">Elizabeth</a> (1364\xe2\x80\x931426)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/John_Hastings,_3rd_Earl_of_Pembroke" title="John Hastings, 3rd Earl of Pembroke">John Hastings, 3rd Earl of Pembroke</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Holland,_1st_Duke_of_Exeter" title="John Holland, 1st Duke of Exeter">John Holland, 1st Duke of Exeter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Cornwall,_1st_Baron_Fanhope" title="John Cornwall, 1st Baron Fanhope">John Cornwall, 1st Baron Fanhope</a>, respectively.</li>\n<li>Edward of Lancaster (1365\xe2\x80\x931365)</li>\n<li>John of Lancaster (1366)\xe2\x80\x94died as an infant.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_England" title="Henry IV of England">Henry</a> (1367\xe2\x80\x931413)</li>\n<li>Isabella of Lancaster (b. 1368)\xe2\x80\x94died as a child.</li></ul></dd>\n<dd>After Blanche\'s death in 1369, John married <a href="/wiki/Constance_of_Castile,_Duchess_of_Lancaster" title="Constance of Castile, Duchess of Lancaster">Constance of Castile</a>, trying unsuccessfully to obtain the throne of Castile. The marriage produced two children:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Lancaster" title="Catherine of Lancaster">Catherine of Lancaster</a> (1372\xe2\x80\x931418)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_Castile" title="Henry III of Castile">Henry III of Castile</a>, with whom she was a great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">Catherine of Aragon</a>, first wife of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII of England</a>.</li>\n<li>John (1374\xe2\x80\x931375)</li></ul></dd>\n<dd>Constance died in 1394, after which John married <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Swynford" title="Katherine Swynford">Katherine Swynford</a> on 13 January 1396. Their four children were born before they married. The pope legitimised them in 1396, as did Richard II by charter, on the condition that their children could not ascend the throne:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_Beaufort,_1st_Earl_of_Somerset" title="John Beaufort, 1st Earl of Somerset">John</a> (c. 1371/1372\xe2\x80\x931410)\xe2\x80\x94grandfather of <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Beaufort,_Countess_of_Richmond_and_Derby" class="mw-redirect" title="Margaret Beaufort, Countess of Richmond and Derby">Margaret Beaufort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII</a>\'s mother.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_Beaufort" title="Henry Beaufort">Henry</a> (1375\xe2\x80\x931447)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Beaufort,_Duke_of_Exeter" title="Thomas Beaufort, Duke of Exeter">Thomas</a> (1377\xe2\x80\x931427)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joan_Beaufort,_Countess_of_Westmorland" title="Joan Beaufort, Countess of Westmorland">Joan</a> (1379\xe2\x80\x931440)\xe2\x80\x94Joan\'s son, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Neville,_5th_Earl_of_Salisbury" title="Richard Neville, 5th Earl of Salisbury">Richard Neville, 5th Earl of Salisbury</a>, and her grandson, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Neville,_16th_Earl_of_Warwick" title="Richard Neville, 16th Earl of Warwick">Richard Neville, 16th Earl of Warwick</a>, were leading supporters of the House of York.</li></ul></dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Edmund_of_Langley,_1st_Duke_of_York" title="Edmund of Langley, 1st Duke of York">Edmund</a> (1341\xe2\x80\x931402)\xe2\x80\x94founder of the House of York. He had three children with <a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Castile,_Duchess_of_York" title="Isabella of Castile, Duchess of York">Isabella of Castile</a>:</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Edward_of_Norwich,_2nd_Duke_of_York" title="Edward of Norwich, 2nd Duke of York">Edward</a> (1373\xe2\x80\x931415)\xe2\x80\x94killed at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Agincourt" title="Battle of Agincourt">Battle of Agincourt</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Constance_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Constance of York">Constance</a> (1374\xe2\x80\x931416)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_of_Conisburgh,_3rd_Earl_of_Cambridge" title="Richard of Conisburgh, 3rd Earl of Cambridge">Richard</a>\xe2\x80\x94(1375\xe2\x80\x931415)</li></ul></dd></dl>\n<ul><li>Blanche (1342)\xe2\x80\x94died as a child.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Waltham" title="Mary of Waltham">Mary of Waltham</a> (1344\xe2\x80\x931362)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/John_V,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="John V, Duke of Brittany">John V, Duke of Brittany</a>. No issue.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Margaret,_Countess_of_Pembroke" title="Margaret, Countess of Pembroke">Margaret</a> (1346\xe2\x80\x931361)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/John_Hastings,_2nd_Earl_of_Pembroke_(4th_Creation)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Hastings, 2nd Earl of Pembroke (4th Creation)">John Hastings, 2nd Earl of Pembroke</a>. No issue.</li>\n<li>Joan (b. 1351)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_of_Woodstock,_1st_Duke_of_Gloucester" title="Thomas of Woodstock, 1st Duke of Gloucester">Thomas</a> (1355\xe2\x80\x931397)\xe2\x80\x94murdered or executed for treason by order of Richard II; his daughter, <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Gloucester" title="Anne of Gloucester">Anne</a>, married <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Stafford,_5th_Earl_of_Stafford" title="Edmund Stafford, 5th Earl of Stafford">Edmund Stafford</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>Edward\xe2\x80\x99s long reign had forged a new national identity, reinforced by Middle English beginning to establish itself as the spoken and written language of government. As a result, he is considered by many historians in cultural respects the first \xe2\x80\x98English\xe2\x80\x99 post-conquest ruler.<sup id="cite_ref-EIIIODNB_76-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIIIODNB-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demise_of_the_main_line">Demise of the main line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demise of the main line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Richard_II_King_of_England.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Medieval painting of King Richard II" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Richard_II_King_of_England.jpg/170px-Richard_II_King_of_England.jpg" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Richard_II_King_of_England.jpg/255px-Richard_II_King_of_England.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/Richard_II_King_of_England.jpg 2x" data-file-width="279" data-file-height="380" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Richard_II_King_of_England.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portrait of <a href="/wiki/Richard_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard II">Richard II</a> (c. 1390). <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>, London.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Black Prince\'s ten-year-old son succeeded as <a href="/wiki/Richard_II_of_England" title="Richard II of England">Richard II of England</a> on the death of his grandfather, nominally exercising all the powers of kingship supported by various councils. His government levied <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_medieval_England" title="Taxation in medieval England">poll taxes</a> to finance military campaigns and combined with the poor state of the economy resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt" title="Peasants&#39; Revolt">Peasants\' Revolt</a> in 1381, followed by brutal reprisals against the rebels.<sup id="cite_ref-RIIODNB_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIIODNB-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The king\'s uncle <a href="/wiki/Thomas_of_Woodstock,_1st_Duke_of_Gloucester" title="Thomas of Woodstock, 1st Duke of Gloucester">Thomas of Woodstock, 1st Duke of Gloucester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_FitzAlan,_11th_Earl_of_Arundel" title="Richard FitzAlan, 11th Earl of Arundel">Richard FitzAlan, 11th Earl of Arundel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_de_Beauchamp,_12th_Earl_of_Warwick" title="Thomas de Beauchamp, 12th Earl of Warwick">Thomas de Beauchamp, 12th Earl of Warwick</a>, became known as the <a href="/wiki/Lords_Appellant" title="Lords Appellant">Lords Appellant</a> when they sought to impeach five of the king\'s favourites and restrain what was increasingly seen as tyrannical and capricious rule. Later they were joined by <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_England" title="Henry IV of England">Henry Bolingbroke</a>, the son and heir of John of Gaunt, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_de_Mowbray,_1st_Duke_of_Norfolk" title="Thomas de Mowbray, 1st Duke of Norfolk">Thomas de Mowbray, 1st Duke of Norfolk</a>. Initially, they were successful in establishing a commission to govern England for one year, but they were forced to rebel against Richard, defeating an army under <a href="/wiki/Robert_de_Vere,_Duke_of_Ireland" title="Robert de Vere, Duke of Ireland">Robert de Vere, Earl of Oxford</a>, at the skirmish of <a href="/wiki/Radcot_Bridge_(Battle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Radcot Bridge (Battle)">Radcot Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RIIODNB_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIIODNB-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Richard was reduced to a figurehead with little power. As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Merciless_Parliament" title="Merciless Parliament">Merciless Parliament</a>, de Vere and <a href="/wiki/Michael_de_la_Pole,_1st_Earl_of_Suffolk" title="Michael de la Pole, 1st Earl of Suffolk">Michael de la Pole, 1st Earl of Suffolk</a>, who had fled abroad, were sentenced to death in their absence. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Neville" title="Alexander Neville">Alexander Neville, Archbishop of York</a>, had all his possessions confiscated. Several of Richard\'s council were executed. On John of Gaunt\'s return from Spain, Richard was able to re-establish his power, having Gloucester murdered in captivity in Calais. Warwick was stripped of his title. Bolingbroke and Mowbray were exiled.<sup id="cite_ref-RIIODNB_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIIODNB-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When John of Gaunt died in 1399, Richard disinherited John\'s son, Henry, who invaded England in response with a small force that quickly grew in numbers. Meeting little resistance, Henry deposed Richard to have himself crowned Henry IV of England. Richard died in captivity early the next year, probably murdered, bringing an end to the main Plantagenet line. None of Henry\'s heirs were free from challenge on the grounds of not being the true heir of Richard II and that the Lancastrian dynasty had gained the throne by an act of usurpation.<sup id="cite_ref-RIIODNB_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIIODNB-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Lancaster">House of Lancaster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: House of Lancaster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lancaster" title="House of Lancaster">House of Lancaster</a></div> <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War_(1415%E2%80%931453)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred Years&#39; War (1415\xe2\x80\x931453)">Hundred Years\' War (1415\xe2\x80\x931453)</a></div>\n<p>Henry married his Plantagenet cousin <a href="/wiki/Mary_de_Bohun" title="Mary de Bohun">Mary de Bohun</a>, who was paternally descended from Edward I and maternally from Edmund Crouchback.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> They had seven children:<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Edward (b. 1382; died as a child)\xe2\x80\x94buried at <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_Castle" title="Monmouth Castle">Monmouth Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monmouth" title="Monmouth">Monmouth</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_V_of_England" title="Henry V of England">Henry</a> (1386\xe2\x80\x931422)\xe2\x80\x94had one son:</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">Henry</a> (1421\xe2\x80\x931471)\xe2\x80\x94also had one son:</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Edward_of_Westminster,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Edward of Westminster, Prince of Wales">Edward</a> (1453\xe2\x80\x931471)</li></ul></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Thomas,_Duke_of_Clarence" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas, Duke of Clarence">Thomas</a> (1387\xe2\x80\x931421)\xe2\x80\x94killed at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baug%C3%A9" title="Battle of Baug\xc3\xa9">Battle of Baug\xc3\xa9</a>. His marriage to <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Holland" class="mw-redirect" title="Margaret Holland">Margaret Holland</a> proved childless; he had an illegitimate son named John, also known as the Bastard of Clarence.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John,_Duke_of_Bedford" class="mw-redirect" title="John, Duke of Bedford">John</a> (1389\xe2\x80\x931435)\xe2\x80\x94had two childless marriages: to <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Burgundy" title="Anne of Burgundy">Anne of Burgundy</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/John_the_Fearless" title="John the Fearless">John the Fearless</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jacquetta_of_Luxembourg" title="Jacquetta of Luxembourg">Jacquetta of Luxembourg</a>. John had an illegitimate son and daughter, named Richard and Mary, respectively.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Humphrey,_Duke_of_Gloucester" title="Humphrey, Duke of Gloucester">Humphrey</a> (1390\xe2\x80\x931447)\xe2\x80\x94died under suspicious circumstances while imprisoned for treason against Henry VI; his death may have been the result of a stroke.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Blanche_of_England" title="Blanche of England">Blanche</a> (1392\xe2\x80\x931409)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Louis_III,_Count_Palatine_of_the_Rhine" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis III, Count Palatine of the Rhine">Louis III, Count Palatine of the Rhine</a>, in 1402.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Philippa_of_England" title="Philippa of England">Philippa</a> (1394\xe2\x80\x931430)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Eric_of_Pomerania" title="Eric of Pomerania">Eric of Pomerania</a>, king of <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, in 1406.</li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet_-_Slag_bij_Azincourt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="15th century illuminated manuscript of the Battle of Agincourt" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet_-_Slag_bij_Azincourt.jpg/170px-Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet_-_Slag_bij_Azincourt.jpg" width="170" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet_-_Slag_bij_Azincourt.jpg/255px-Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet_-_Slag_bij_Azincourt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet_-_Slag_bij_Azincourt.jpg/340px-Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet_-_Slag_bij_Azincourt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="702" data-file-height="952" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet_-_Slag_bij_Azincourt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parchment miniature of Henry V\'s victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Agincourt" title="Battle of Agincourt">Battle of Agincourt</a> in 1415, from <a href="/wiki/Enguerrand_de_Monstrelet" title="Enguerrand de Monstrelet">Enguerrand de Monstrelet</a>\'s <i>Chronique de France</i> circa 1495</div></div></div><p>Henry went to convoluted legal means to justify his succession. Many Lancastrians asserted that his mother had had legitimate rights through her descent from <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Crouchback" title="Edmund Crouchback">Edmund Crouchback</a>, who it was claimed was the elder son of Henry III of England, set aside due to deformity.<sup id="cite_ref-Schama264_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schama264-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> As the great-grandson of <a href="/wiki/Lionel_of_Antwerp,_1st_Duke_of_Clarence" title="Lionel of Antwerp, 1st Duke of Clarence">Lionel of Antwerp, 1st Duke of Clarence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Mortimer,_5th_Earl_of_March" title="Edmund Mortimer, 5th Earl of March">Edmund Mortimer, Earl of March</a>, was the heir presumptive to Richard II and Henry used multiple rationales stressing his Plantagenet descent, divine grace, powerful friends, and Richard\'s misgovernment.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBHIV_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBHIV-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In fact Mortimer never showed interest in the throne. The later marriage of his sister <a href="/wiki/Anne_de_Mortimer" title="Anne de Mortimer">Anne</a> to <a href="/wiki/Richard_of_Conisburgh,_3rd_Earl_of_Cambridge" title="Richard of Conisburgh, 3rd Earl of Cambridge">Richard of Conisburgh, 3rd Earl of Cambridge</a> consolidated this claim to the throne with that of the more junior <a href="/wiki/House_of_York" title="House of York">House of York</a>. Henry planned to resume war with France, but was plagued with financial problems, declining health and frequent rebellions.<sup id="cite_ref-mortimer353_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mortimer353-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> He defeated a Scottish invasion, a serious rebellion by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Percy,_1st_Earl_of_Northumberland" title="Henry Percy, 1st Earl of Northumberland">Henry Percy, 1st Earl of Northumberland</a> in the North and <a href="/wiki/Owain_Glynd%C5%B5r" title="Owain Glynd\xc5\xb5r">Owain Glynd\xc5\xb5r</a>\'s rebellion in Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-mortimer353_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mortimer353-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Many saw it as a punishment from God when Henry was later struck down with unknown but chronic illnesses.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBHIV_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBHIV-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Henry IV died in 1413. His son and successor, <a href="/wiki/Henry_V_of_England" title="Henry V of England">Henry V of England</a>, aware that <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI_of_France" title="Charles VI of France">Charles VI of France</a>\'s mental illness had caused instability in France, invaded to assert the Plantagenet claims and won a near total victory over the French at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Agincourt" title="Battle of Agincourt">Battle of Agincourt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Schama265_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schama265-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In subsequent years Henry recaptured much of Normandy and secured marriage to <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Valois" title="Catherine of Valois">Catherine of Valois</a>. The resulting <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Troyes" title="Treaty of Troyes">Treaty of Troyes</a> stated that Henry\'s heirs would inherit the throne of France, but conflict continued with <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII_of_France" title="Charles VII of France">the Dauphin</a>. When Henry died in 1422, his nine-month-old son succeeded him as <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">Henry VI of England</a>.  During the minority of Henry VI the war caused political division among his Plantagenet uncles, Bedford, <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_of_Lancaster,_1st_Duke_of_Gloucester" class="mw-redirect" title="Humphrey of Lancaster, 1st Duke of Gloucester">Humphrey of Lancaster, 1st Duke of Gloucester</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Beaufort" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal Beaufort">Cardinal Beaufort</a>. Humphrey\'s wife was accused of treasonable <a href="/wiki/Necromancy" title="Necromancy">necromancy</a> after two astrologers in her employ unwisely, if honestly, predicted a serious illness would endanger Henry VI\'s life, and Humphrey was later arrested and died in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Depopulation stemming from the Black Death led to increased wages, static food costs and a resulting improvement in the standard of living for the peasantry. However, under Henry misgovernment and harvest failures depressed the English economy to a pitiful state known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Slump_(15th_century)" title="Great Slump (15th century)">Great Slump</a>. The economy was in ruins by 1450, a consequence of the loss of France, piracy in the channel and poor trading relations with the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The economic slowdown began in the 1430s in the north of the country, spreading south in the 1440s, with the economy not recovering until the 1480s.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> It was also driven by multiple harvest failures in the 1430s and disease amongst livestock, which drove up the price of food and damaged the wider economy.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Certain groups were particularly badly affected: cloth exports fell by 35 per cent in just four years at the end of the 1440s, collapsing by up to 90 per cent in some parts of the South-West.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The Crown\'s debts reached \xc2\xa3372,000, Henry\'s deficit was \xc2\xa320,000 per annum, and tax revenues were half those of his father.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_York">House of York</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: House of York">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/House_of_York" title="House of York">House of York</a></div> <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a></div>\n<p>Edward III made his fourth son Edmund the first <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_York" title="Duke of York">duke of York</a> in 1362. Edmund was married to Isabella, a daughter of King Peter of Castile and <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_de_Padilla" title="Mar\xc3\xada de Padilla">Mar\xc3\xada de Padilla</a> and the sister of Constance of Castile, who was the second wife of Edmund\'s brother John of Gaunt. Both of Edmund\'s sons were killed in 1415. <a href="/wiki/Richard_of_Conisburgh,_3rd_Earl_of_Cambridge" title="Richard of Conisburgh, 3rd Earl of Cambridge">Richard</a> became involved in the <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Plot" title="Southampton Plot">Southampton Plot</a>, a conspiracy to depose Henry V in favour of Richard\'s brother-in-law Edmund Mortimer. When Mortimer revealed the plot to the king, Richard was executed for treason. Richard\'s childless older brother <a href="/wiki/Edward_of_Norwich,_2nd_Duke_of_York" title="Edward of Norwich, 2nd Duke of York">Edward</a> was killed at the Battle of Agincourt later the same year. <a href="/wiki/Constance_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Constance of York">Constance of York</a> was Edmund\'s only daughter and was an ancestor of Queen <a href="/wiki/Anne_Neville" title="Anne Neville">Anne Neville</a>. The increasingly interwoven Plantagenet relationships were demonstrated by Edmund\'s second marriage to <a href="/wiki/Joan_Holland" title="Joan Holland">Joan Holland</a>. Her sister <a href="/wiki/Alianore_Holland,_Countess_of_March" title="Alianore Holland, Countess of March">Alianore Holland</a> was mother to Richard\'s wife, Anne Mortimer. <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Holland" class="mw-redirect" title="Margaret Holland">Margaret Holland</a>, another of Joan\'s sisters, married <a href="/wiki/John_Beaufort,_1st_Earl_of_Somerset" title="John Beaufort, 1st Earl of Somerset">John of Gaunt\'s son</a>. She later married <a href="/wiki/Thomas_of_Lancaster,_1st_Duke_of_Clarence" title="Thomas of Lancaster, 1st Duke of Clarence">Thomas of Lancaster</a>, John of Gaunt\'s grandson by King Henry IV. A third sister, <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Holland,_Countess_of_Salisbury" title="Eleanor Holland, Countess of Salisbury">Eleanor Holland</a>, was mother-in-law to <a href="/wiki/Richard_Neville,_5th_Earl_of_Salisbury" title="Richard Neville, 5th Earl of Salisbury">Richard Neville, 5th Earl of Salisbury</a>\xe2\x80\x94John\'s grandson by his daughter <a href="/wiki/Joan_Beaufort,_Countess_of_Westmorland" title="Joan Beaufort, Countess of Westmorland">Joan Beaufort, Countess of Westmorland</a>. These sisters were all granddaughters of Joan of Kent, the mother of Richard II, and therefore Plantagenet descendants of Edward I.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Edmund\'s son Richard was married to Anne Mortimer, the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Roger_Mortimer,_4th_Earl_of_March" title="Roger Mortimer, 4th Earl of March">Roger Mortimer, 4th Earl of March</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alianore_Holland" class="mw-redirect" title="Alianore Holland">Eleanor Holland</a> and great-granddaughter of Edward III\'s second surviving son Lionel. Anne died giving birth to their only son in September 1411.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Richard\'s execution four years later left two orphans: <a href="/wiki/Isabel_of_Cambridge,_Countess_of_Essex" title="Isabel of Cambridge, Countess of Essex">Isabel</a>, who married into the Bourchier family, and a son who was also called Richard. Although his earldom was forfeited, Richard (the father) was not <a href="/wiki/Attainder" title="Attainder">attainted</a>, and the four-year-old orphan Richard was his heir. Within months of his father\'s death, Richard\'s childless uncle, Edward Duke of York, was killed at Agincourt. Richard was allowed to inherit the title of Duke of York in 1426. In 1432 he acquired the earldoms of March and Ulster on the death of his maternal uncle Edmund Mortimer, Earl of March, who had died campaigning with Henry V in France, and the earldom of Cambridge which had belonged to his father. Being descended from Edward III in both the maternal and the paternal line gave Richard a significant claim to the throne if the Lancastrian line should fail, and by <a href="/wiki/Cognatic_primogeniture" class="mw-redirect" title="Cognatic primogeniture">cognatic primogeniture</a> arguably a superior claim.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBRoY_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBRoY-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>  He emphasised the point by being the first to assume the Plantagenet surname in 1448. Having inherited the March and Ulster titles, he became the wealthiest and most powerful noble in England, second only to the king himself. Richard married <a href="/wiki/Cecily_Neville,_Duchess_of_York" title="Cecily Neville, Duchess of York">Cecily Neville</a>, a granddaughter of John of Gaunt, and had thirteen or possibly fifteen children:<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Joan (b. 1438; died as a child)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anne_of_York,_Duchess_of_Exeter" title="Anne of York, Duchess of Exeter">Anne of York</a> (1439\xe2\x80\x931476)\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Mitochondrial_DNA" title="Mitochondrial DNA">Mitochondrial DNA</a> taken from a descendant of her second daughter, <a href="/wiki/Anne_St_Leger,_Baroness_de_Ros" title="Anne St Leger, Baroness de Ros">Anne St Leger, Baroness de Ros</a>, was used in the identification of <a href="/wiki/Exhumation_of_Richard_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Exhumation of Richard III">the remains of Richard III</a>, which were found in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Henry (b. 1441; died as a child)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edward_IV_of_England" title="Edward IV of England">Edward</a> (1442\xe2\x80\x931483)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edmund,_Earl_of_Rutland" title="Edmund, Earl of Rutland">Edmund</a> (1443\xe2\x80\x931460)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_York,_Duchess_of_Suffolk" title="Elizabeth of York, Duchess of Suffolk">Elizabeth</a> (1444\xe2\x80\x931503)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/John_de_la_Pole,_2nd_Duke_of_Suffolk" title="John de la Pole, 2nd Duke of Suffolk">John de la Pole, 2nd Duke of Suffolk</a>; she was the mother of several claimants to the throne.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_York" title="Margaret of York">Margaret</a> (1446\xe2\x80\x931503)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Bold" title="Charles the Bold">Charles the Bold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Burgundy" title="Duke of Burgundy">Duke of Burgundy</a>.</li>\n<li>William (b. 1447; died as a child)</li>\n<li>John (b. 1448; died as a child)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_Plantagenet,_1st_Duke_of_Clarence" title="George Plantagenet, 1st Duke of Clarence">George</a> (1449\xe2\x80\x931478)</li>\n<li>Thomas (b. 1450/51; died as a child)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_III_of_England" title="Richard III of England">Richard</a> (1452\xe2\x80\x931485)</li>\n<li>Ursula (b. 1455; died as a child)</li>\n<li>In her will, Cecily stated that Katherine and Humphrey were her children, but they may have been her grandchildren through de la Pole.</li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MS_Ghent_-_Battle_of_Tewkesbury.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The Battle of Tewkesbury, as illustrated in the Ghent manuscript" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/MS_Ghent_-_Battle_of_Tewkesbury.jpg/170px-MS_Ghent_-_Battle_of_Tewkesbury.jpg" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/MS_Ghent_-_Battle_of_Tewkesbury.jpg/255px-MS_Ghent_-_Battle_of_Tewkesbury.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/MS_Ghent_-_Battle_of_Tewkesbury.jpg/340px-MS_Ghent_-_Battle_of_Tewkesbury.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1496" data-file-height="1738" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MS_Ghent_-_Battle_of_Tewkesbury.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Battle_of_Tewkesbury" class="mw-redirect" title="The Battle of Tewkesbury">The Battle of Tewkesbury</a>, as illustrated in the Ghent manuscript</div></div></div><p>When Henry VI had a mental breakdown, Richard was named regent, but the birth of a male heir resolved the question of succession.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBRoY_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBRoY-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>  When Henry\'s sanity returned, the court party reasserted its authority, but Richard of York and the Nevilles defeated them at a skirmish called the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_St_Albans" title="First Battle of St Albans">First Battle of St Albans</a>. The ruling class was deeply shocked and reconciliation was attempted.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBRoY_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBRoY-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> York and the Nevilles fled abroad, but the Nevilles returned to win the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Northampton_(1460)" title="Battle of Northampton (1460)">Battle of Northampton</a>, where they captured Henry.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBRoY_97-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBRoY-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> When Richard of York joined them he surprised Parliament by claiming the throne and forcing through the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Accord" title="Act of Accord">Act of Accord</a>, which stated that Henry would remain as king for his lifetime, but would be succeeded by York. Margaret found this disregard for her son\'s claims unacceptable, and so the conflict continued. York was killed at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wakefield" title="Battle of Wakefield">Battle of Wakefield</a> and his head set on display at <a href="/wiki/Micklegate_Bar" class="mw-redirect" title="Micklegate Bar">Micklegate Bar</a> along with those of <a href="/wiki/Edmund,_Earl_of_Rutland" title="Edmund, Earl of Rutland">Edmund, Earl of Rutland</a>, and Richard Neville, Earl of Salisbury, who had been captured and beheaded.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBRoY_97-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBRoY-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The Scottish queen <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Guelders" title="Mary of Guelders">Mary of Guelders</a> provided Margaret with support but London welcomed York\'s son <a href="/wiki/Edward_IV_of_England" title="Edward IV of England">Edward, Earl of March</a> and Parliament confirmed that Edward should be made king. He was crowned after consolidating his position with victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Towton" title="Battle of Towton">Battle of Towton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBEIV_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBEIV-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Edward\'s preferment of the former Lancastrian-supporting Woodville family, following his marriage to <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Woodville" title="Elizabeth Woodville">Elizabeth Woodville</a>, led Warwick and Clarence to help Margaret depose Edward and return Henry to the throne. Edward and <a href="/wiki/Richard_III_of_England" title="Richard III of England">Richard, Duke of Gloucester</a>, fled, but on their return, Clarence switched sides at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Barnet" title="Battle of Barnet">Battle of Barnet</a>, leading to the death of the Neville brothers. The subsequent <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tewkesbury" title="Battle of Tewkesbury">Battle of Tewkesbury</a> brought the demise of the last of the male line of the Beauforts. The battlefield execution of <a href="/wiki/Edward_of_Westminster,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Edward of Westminster, Prince of Wales">Edward of Westminster, Prince of Wales</a>, and the later probable murder of Henry VI extinguished the House of Lancaster.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the mid-1470s, the victorious House of York looked safely established, with seven living male princes: Edward IV and his two sons, his brother George and George\'s son, his brother Richard and Richard\'s son. Edward and Elizabeth Woodville themselves had ten children, seven of whom survived him:<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_York" title="Elizabeth of York">Elizabeth</a> (1466\xe2\x80\x931503)\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Queen_consort" title="Queen consort">queen consort</a> to <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mary_of_York" title="Mary of York">Mary</a> (1467\xe2\x80\x931482)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cecily_of_York" title="Cecily of York">Cecily</a> (1469\xe2\x80\x931507)\xe2\x80\x94initially married <a href="/wiki/John_Welles,_1st_Viscount_Welles" title="John Welles, 1st Viscount Welles">John Welles, 1st Viscount Welles</a>, and later married Thomas Kyme (or Keme) following John\'s death.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edward_V_of_England" title="Edward V of England">Edward</a> (1470\xe2\x80\x93c. 1483)\xe2\x80\x94briefly succeeded his father as King Edward V.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_York_(1472)" title="Margaret of York (1472)">Margaret</a> (1472; died that year)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_of_Shrewsbury,_Duke_of_York" title="Richard of Shrewsbury, Duke of York">Richard</a> (1473\xe2\x80\x93c. 1483)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anne_of_York_(daughter_of_Edward_IV)" title="Anne of York (daughter of Edward IV)">Anne</a> (1475\xe2\x80\x931511)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Howard,_3rd_Duke_of_Norfolk" title="Thomas Howard, 3rd Duke of Norfolk">Thomas Howard</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_Plantagenet,_1st_Duke_of_Bedford" title="George Plantagenet, 1st Duke of Bedford">George</a> (1477\xe2\x80\x931479)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_York" title="Catherine of York">Catherine of York</a> (1479\xe2\x80\x931527)\xe2\x80\x94married <a href="/wiki/William_Courtenay,_1st_Earl_of_Devon" title="William Courtenay, 1st Earl of Devon">William Courtenay, 1st Earl of Devon</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bridget_of_York" title="Bridget of York">Bridget of York</a> (1480\xe2\x80\x931517)\xe2\x80\x94became a nun \xe2\x80\x94 possibly had an illegitimate daughter called <a href="/wiki/Agnes_of_Eltham" title="Agnes of Eltham">Agnes of Eltham</a></li></ul>\n<p>Dynastic infighting and misfortune quickly brought about the demise of the House of York. <a href="/wiki/George_Plantagenet,_1st_Duke_of_Clarence" title="George Plantagenet, 1st Duke of Clarence">George Plantagenet, 1st Duke of Clarence</a>, plotted against his brother and was executed. Following Edward\'s premature death in 1483, his brother Richard had Parliament declare Edward\'s two sons illegitimate on the pretext of an alleged prior pre-contract to <a href="/wiki/Lady_Eleanor_Talbot" title="Lady Eleanor Talbot">Lady Eleanor Talbot</a>, leaving Edward\'s marriage invalid.<sup id="cite_ref-RIIIODNB_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIIIODNB-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Richard seized the throne, and the <a href="/wiki/Princes_in_the_Tower" title="Princes in the Tower">Princes in the Tower</a> were never seen again. Richard\'s son predeceased him and Richard was killed in 1485<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> after an invasion of foreign mercenaries led by <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry Tudor</a>, who claimed the throne through his mother <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Beaufort,_Countess_of_Richmond_and_Derby" class="mw-redirect" title="Margaret Beaufort, Countess of Richmond and Derby">Margaret Beaufort</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Tudor assumed the throne as Henry VII, founding the Tudor dynasty and bringing the Plantagenet line of kings to an end.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Tudor_and_other_Plantagenet_descendants">House of Tudor and other Plantagenet descendants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: House of Tudor and other Plantagenet descendants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_of_York_from_Kings_and_Queens_of_England.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Portrait of Elizabeth of York (1465\xe2\x80\x931503)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Elizabeth_of_York_from_Kings_and_Queens_of_England.jpg/170px-Elizabeth_of_York_from_Kings_and_Queens_of_England.jpg" width="170" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Elizabeth_of_York_from_Kings_and_Queens_of_England.jpg/255px-Elizabeth_of_York_from_Kings_and_Queens_of_England.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Elizabeth_of_York_from_Kings_and_Queens_of_England.jpg/340px-Elizabeth_of_York_from_Kings_and_Queens_of_England.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1318" data-file-height="1816" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_of_York_from_Kings_and_Queens_of_England.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_York" title="Elizabeth of York">Elizabeth of York</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tudor">Tudor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tudor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>When Henry Tudor seized the throne there were eighteen Plantagenet descendants who might today be thought to have a stronger hereditary claim, and by 1510 this number had been increased further by the birth of sixteen Yorkist children.<sup id="cite_ref-Weir2008p148_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weir2008p148-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>  Henry mitigated this situation with his marriage to <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_York" title="Elizabeth of York">Elizabeth of York</a>. She was the eldest daughter of Edward IV, and all their children were his cognatic heirs. Indeed, <a href="/wiki/Polydore_Vergil" title="Polydore Vergil">Polydore Vergil</a> noted Henry VIII\'s pronounced resemblance to his grandfather Edward: "For just as Edward was the most warmly thought of by the English people amongst all English kings, so this successor of his, Henry, was very much like him in general appearance, in greatness of mind and generosity and for that reason was the most acclaimed and approved of all."<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This did not deter <a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_York" title="Margaret of York">Margaret of York, Duchess of Burgundy</a>\xe2\x80\x94Edward\'s sister and Elizabeth\'s aunt\xe2\x80\x94and members of the de la Pole family\xe2\x80\x94children of Edward\'s sister and <a href="/wiki/John_de_la_Pole,_2nd_Duke_of_Suffolk" title="John de la Pole, 2nd Duke of Suffolk">John de la Pole, 2nd Duke of Suffolk</a>\xe2\x80\x94 from frequent attempts to destabilise Henry\'s regime.<sup id="cite_ref-ODNBMoY_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODNBMoY-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Henry imprisoned Margaret\'s nephew <a href="/wiki/Edward_Plantagenet,_17th_Earl_of_Warwick" title="Edward Plantagenet, 17th Earl of Warwick">Edward, Earl of Warwick</a>, the son of her brother George, in the Tower of London, but in 1487 Margaret financed a rebellion led by <a href="/wiki/Lambert_Simnel" title="Lambert Simnel">Lambert Simnel</a> pretending to be Edward. <a href="/wiki/John_de_la_Pole,_1st_Earl_of_Lincoln" title="John de la Pole, 1st Earl of Lincoln">John de la Pole, 1st Earl of Lincoln</a>, joined the revolt, probably anticipating that it would further his own ambitions to the throne, but he was killed in the suppression of the uprising at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stoke_Field" title="Battle of Stoke Field">Battle of Stoke Field</a> in 1487.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Warwick was implicated by two further failed invasions supported by Margaret using <a href="/wiki/Perkin_Warbeck" title="Perkin Warbeck">Perkin Warbeck</a> pretending to be Edward IV\'s son Richard of Shrewsbury, and Warbeck\'s later planned escape for them both; Warwick was executed in 1499. Edward\'s execution may simply have been a precondition for the marriage of <a href="/wiki/Arthur,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Arthur, Prince of Wales">Arthur, Prince of Wales</a> to <a href="/wiki/Katherine_of_Aragon" class="mw-redirect" title="Katherine of Aragon">Katherine of Aragon</a> in 1501.<sup id="cite_ref-EEoW_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEoW-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="De_La_Pole">De La Pole</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: De La Pole">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>John de la Pole\'s attainder meant that his brother Edmund inherited their father\'s titles, but much of the wealth of the duchy of Suffolk was forfeit. Edmund did not possess sufficient finances to maintain his status as a duke, so as a compromise he accepted the title of earl of Suffolk. Financial difficulties led to frequent legal conflicts and Edmund\'s indictment for murder in 1501. He fled with his brother Richard, while their remaining brother, William, was imprisoned in the Tower\xe2\x80\x94where he would remain until his death 37 years later\xe2\x80\x94as part of a general suppression of Edmund\'s associates <a href="/wiki/Philip_I_of_Castile" title="Philip I of Castile">Philip the Fair</a> had been holding Edmund and in 1506 he returned him to Henry. Edmund was imprisoned in the Tower. In 1513, he was executed after Richard de la Pole, whom <a href="/wiki/Louis_XII_of_France" title="Louis XII of France">Louis XII of France</a> had recognised as king of England the previous year, claimed the kingship in his own right.<sup id="cite_ref-EDLP_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDLP-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Richard, known as the White Rose, plotted an invasion of England for years but was killed in 1525 at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pavia" title="Battle of Pavia">Battle of Pavia</a> while fighting as the captain of the French <a href="/wiki/Landsknechts" class="mw-redirect" title="Landsknechts">landsknechts</a> during <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_I_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois I of France">Fran\xc3\xa7ois I of France</a>\'s invasion of Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-RDLP_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RDLP-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pole">Pole</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Pole">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reginald_Pole_from_NPG.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ancient oil painting of Cardinal Pole" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Reginald_Pole_from_NPG.jpg/170px-Reginald_Pole_from_NPG.jpg" width="170" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Reginald_Pole_from_NPG.jpg/255px-Reginald_Pole_from_NPG.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Reginald_Pole_from_NPG.jpg/340px-Reginald_Pole_from_NPG.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3060" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reginald_Pole_from_NPG.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Pole" title="Reginald Pole">Reginald Pole</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Warwick\'s sister, and therefore Edward IV\'s niece, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Pole,_Countess_of_Salisbury" title="Margaret Pole, Countess of Salisbury">Margaret Pole, Countess of Salisbury</a>, was executed by Henry VIII in 1541. By then, the cause was more religious and political rather than dynastic. The attainder of her father, <a href="/wiki/George_Plantagenet,_1st_Duke_of_Clarence" title="George Plantagenet, 1st Duke of Clarence">Clarence</a>, was a legal bar to any claims to the throne by his children. Additionally her marriage, arranged by Henry VII, to <a href="/wiki/Sir_Richard_Pole" title="Sir Richard Pole">Sir Richard Pole</a>, his half-cousin and trusted supporter, was not auspicious. Nevertheless, it did allow the couple to be closely involved in court affairs. Margaret\'s fortunes improved under Henry VIII and in February 1512 she was restored to the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Salisbury" title="Earl of Salisbury">earldom of Salisbury</a> and all the Warwicks\' lands. This made her the first and, apart from <a href="/wiki/Anne_Boleyn" title="Anne Boleyn">Anne Boleyn</a>, the only woman in 16th-century England to hold a peerage title in her own right.<sup id="cite_ref-Pole_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pole-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Her daughter <a href="/wiki/Ursula_Pole,_Baroness_Stafford" title="Ursula Pole, Baroness Stafford">Ursula</a> married the son of <a href="/wiki/Edward_Stafford,_3rd_Duke_of_Buckingham" title="Edward Stafford, 3rd Duke of Buckingham">Edward Stafford, 3rd Duke of Buckingham</a>. Buckingham\'s fall after arguments with the king over property, and Margaret\'s open support for <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">Catherine of Aragon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">Princess Mary</a> began the Poles\' estrangement from the king. Hope of reconciliation was dashed by <i>De unitate</i>, the letter that Margaret\'s son <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Pole" title="Reginald Pole">Reginald Pole</a> wrote to Henry VIII, in which Reginald declared his opposition to the royal supremacy. In 1538 evidence came to light that Pole family members in England had been in communication with Reginald. Margaret\'s sons <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Pole" title="Geoffrey Pole">Geoffrey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Pole,_1st_Baron_Montagu" title="Henry Pole, 1st Baron Montagu">Henry</a> were arrested for treason along with several friends and associates, including Henry\'s wife and brother-in-law\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Sir_Edward_Neville" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Edward Neville">Edward Neville</a>. Among those arrested was the king\'s cousin <a href="/wiki/Henry_Courtenay,_1st_Marquess_of_Exeter" title="Henry Courtenay, 1st Marquess of Exeter">Henry Courtenay, 1st Marquess of Exeter</a>, his wife and 11-year-old son. Courteney\'s wife was released two years later, but their son spent 15 years in the Tower until Queen Mary released him. Except for the surviving Geoffrey Pole, all the others implicated were beheaded.<sup id="cite_ref-Courteney_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Courteney-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Margaret was attainted. The possibility of an invasion involving Reginald via her south coast estates and her embittered relationship with Henry VIII precluded any chance of pardon. However, the decision to execute her seems a spontaneous, rather than a premeditated, act. According to the Calendar of State Papers her execution was botched at the hands of "a wretched and blundering youth&#160;... who literally hacked her head and shoulders to pieces in the most pitiful manner". In 1886 she was beatified by Pope <a href="/wiki/Leo_XIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Leo XIII">Leo XIII</a> on the grounds she had laid down her life for the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> "and for the truth of the orthodox Faith".<sup id="cite_ref-Pole_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pole-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stafford">Stafford</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Stafford">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Edward Stafford,  Duke of Buckingham, combined multiple lines of Plantagenet descent: from Edward III by his son Thomas of Woodstock, from Edward III via two of his Beaufort grandchildren, and from Edward I from Joan of Kent and the <a href="/wiki/Holland_family" title="Holland family">Holland family</a>. His father failed in his rebellion against Richard III in 1483 but was restored to his inheritance on the reversal of his father\'s attainder late in 1485. His mother married Henry VII\'s uncle <a href="/wiki/Jasper_Tudor" class="mw-redirect" title="Jasper Tudor">Jasper Tudor</a>, and his wardship was entrusted to the king\'s mother, <a href="/wiki/Lady_Margaret_Beaufort" title="Lady Margaret Beaufort">Lady Margaret Beaufort</a>. In 1502, during Henry VII\'s illness, there was debate as to whether Buckingham or Edmund de la Pole should act as regent for Henry VIII. There is no evidence of continuous hostility between Buckingham and Henry VIII, but there is little doubt of the duke\'s dislike of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wolsey" title="Thomas Wolsey">Thomas Wolsey</a>, whom he believed to be plotting to ruin the old nobility. Therefore, Henry VIII instructed Wolsey to watch Buckingham, his brother <a href="/wiki/Henry_Stafford,_1st_Earl_of_Wiltshire" title="Henry Stafford, 1st Earl of Wiltshire">Henry Stafford, 1st Earl of Wiltshire</a>, and three other peers. Neither Henry VIII nor his father planned to destroy Buckingham because of his lineage and Henry VIII even allowed Buckingham\'s son and heir, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Stafford,_1st_Baron_Stafford" title="Henry Stafford, 1st Baron Stafford">Henry Stafford, 1st Baron Stafford</a>, to marry Ursula Pole, giving the Staffords a further line of royal blood descent. Buckingham himself was arrested in April 1521; he was found guilty on 16 May and executed the next day. Evidence was provided that the duke had been listening to prophecies that he would be king and that the Tudor family lay under God\'s curse for the execution of Warwick. This was said to explain Henry VIII\'s failure to produce a male heir. Much of this evidence consisted of ill-judged comments, speculation and bad temper, but it underlined the threat presented by Buckingham\'s descent.<sup id="cite_ref-Stafford_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stafford-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tudor_succession">Tudor succession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tudor succession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Succession_to_Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Succession to Elizabeth I of England">Succession to Elizabeth I of England</a></div>\n<p>As late as 1600, with the Tudor succession in doubt, older Plantagenet lines remained as possible claimants to a disputed throne, and religious and dynastic factors gave rise to complications. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wilson_(record_keeper)" title="Thomas Wilson (record keeper)">Thomas Wilson</a> wrote in his report <i>The State of England, Anno Domini 1600</i> that there were 12 "competitors" for the succession. At the time of writing (about 1601), Wilson had been working on intelligence matters for <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sackville,_1st_Earl_of_Dorset" title="Thomas Sackville, 1st Earl of Dorset">Lord Buckhurst</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sir_Robert_Cecil" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Robert Cecil">Sir Robert Cecil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WilsonTom_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WilsonTom-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\nThe alleged competitors included five descendants of Henry VII and Elizabeth, including the eventual successor <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="James I of England">James I of England</a>, but also seven from older Plantagenet lines:<sup id="cite_ref-Pro_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pro-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Henry_Hastings,_3rd_Earl_of_Huntingdon" title="Henry Hastings, 3rd Earl of Huntingdon">Henry Hastings, 3rd Earl of Huntingdon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_Hastings,_4th_Earl_of_Huntingdon" title="George Hastings, 4th Earl of Huntingdon">George Hastings, 4th Earl of Huntingdon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Neville,_6th_Earl_of_Westmorland" title="Charles Neville, 6th Earl of Westmorland">Charles Neville, 6th Earl of Westmorland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_Percy,_9th_Earl_of_Northumberland" title="Henry Percy, 9th Earl of Northumberland">Henry Percy, 9th Earl of Northumberland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio,_Prior_of_Crato" title="Ant\xc3\xb3nio, Prior of Crato">Ant\xc3\xb3nio, Prior of Crato</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ranuccio_I_Farnese,_Duke_of_Parma" title="Ranuccio I Farnese, Duke of Parma">Ranuccio I Farnese, Duke of Parma</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Philip_III_of_Spain" title="Philip III of Spain">Philip III of Spain</a> and his infant daughter</li></ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Ranulph_Crewe" title="Ranulph Crewe">Ranulph Crewe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chief_Justice_of_England_and_Wales" title="Lord Chief Justice of England and Wales">Chief Justice of the King\'s Bench</a>, argued that by 1626 the House of Plantagenet could not be considered to remain in existence in a speech during the Oxford Peerage case, which was to rule on who should inherit the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Oxford" title="Earl of Oxford">earldom of Oxford</a>. It was referred by <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I of England</a> to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, who called for judicial assistance. Crewe said:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>I have labored to make a covenant with myself, that affection may not press upon judgment; for I suppose there is no man that hath any apprehension of gentry or nobleness, but his affection stands to the continuance of a house so illustrious, and would take hold of a twig or twine-thread to support it. And yet time hath his revolutions; there must be a period and an end to all temporal things\xe2\x80\x94finis rerum\xe2\x80\x94an end of names and dignities, and whatsoever is terrene; and why not of <a href="/wiki/De_Vere_family" title="De Vere family">de Vere</a>? For where is <a href="/wiki/Bohun_family" title="Bohun family">Bohun</a>? Where is <a href="/wiki/House_of_Mowbray" title="House of Mowbray">Mowbray</a>? Where is <a href="/wiki/Mortimer" title="Mortimer">Mortimer</a>? Nay, which is more, and most of all, where is Plantagenet? They are entombed in the urns and sepulchres of mortality! yet let the name of de Vere stand so long as it pleaseth God.<sup id="cite_ref-carew_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carew-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genealogy">Genealogy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Genealogy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/English_monarchs_family_tree#House_of_Plantagenet" class="mw-redirect" title="English monarchs family tree">Plantagenet monarchs\' family tree</a></div>\n<div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" females)</div><div class="mw-collapsible-content" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;">\n<p><b>Angevins</b><sup id="cite_ref-Angevins_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angevins-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">Henry II of England</a>, 1133\xe2\x80\x931189, had 5 sons;\n</p>\n<dl><dd>1. <a href="/wiki/William_IX,_Count_of_Poitiers" title="William IX, Count of Poitiers">William IX, Count of Poitiers</a>, 1153\xe2\x80\x931156, died in infancy</dd>\n<dd>2. <a England">Richard I of England</a>, 1157\xe2\x80\x931199, died without legitimate issue</dd>\n<dd>4. <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey,_Duke_of_Brittany" class="mw-redirect" title="Geoffrey, Duke of Brittany">Geoffrey, Duke of Brittany</a>, 1158\xe2\x80\x931186, had 1 son;\n<dl><dd>A. <a href="/wiki/Arthur_I,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Arthur I, Duke of Brittany">Arthur I, Duke of Brittany</a>, 1187\xe2\x80\x931203, died without issue</dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>5. <a href="/wiki/John_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="John of England">John of England</a>, 1167\xe2\x80\x931216, had 2 sons;</dd></dl>\n<p><b>Plantagenets</b><sup id="cite_ref-Plantagenets_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plantagenets-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd>A. <a Edward, 1365\xe2\x80\x931372, died young</dd>\n<dd>B. <a href="/wiki/Richard_II_of_England" title="Richard II of England">Richard II of England</a>, 1367\xe2\x80\x931400, died without issue</dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>2. William of Hatfield, 1337\xe2\x80\x931337, died in infancy</dd>\n<dd>3. <a href="/wiki/Lionel_of_Antwerp,_1st_Duke_of_Clarence" title="Lionel of Antwerp, 1st Duke of Clarence">Lionel of Antwerp, 1st href="/wiki/Philippa,_5th_Countess_of_Ulster" title="Philippa, 5th Countess of Ulster">Philippa, 5th Countess of Ulster</a>, 1355\xe2\x80\x931381, married <a title="Elizabeth Mortimer">Elizabeth Mortimer</a>, 1371\xe2\x80\x931417 married <a href="/wiki/Henry_Percy_(Hotspur)" title="Henry Percy (Hotspur)">Henry Percy (Hotspur)</a>, 1 son, 2 daughter\n<dl><dd><b>To the Earls of Northumberland</b><sup id="cite_ref-Northumberland_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Northumberland-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>II <a href="/wiki/Roger_Mortimer,_4th_Earl_of_March" title="Roger Mortimer, 4th Earl of March">Roger Mortimer, 4th Earl of March</a>, 1373\xe2\x80\x931398, married Eleanor daughter of <a 3rd Earl of Cambridge">Richard of Conisburgh, 3rd Earl of Cambridge</a> (see below) and it is through her descent from Lionel that the House of York claimed precedence over the House of Lancaster.</dd>\n<dd><b>To the <a href="/wiki/House_of_York" title="House of York">House of York</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-YorkAnne_125-0" class="reference"><a Francis Somerset</dd>\n<dd>C. Charles Somerset</dd>\n<dd>D. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Somerset" title="Thomas Somerset">Thomas Somerset</a></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>b. <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Beaufort,_4th_Duke_of_Somerset" class="mw-redirect" title="Edmund Beaufort, 4th Duke of Somerset">Edmund Beaufort, 4th Duke of Somerset</a>, 1439\xe2\x80\x931471, died without issue</dd>\n<dd>c. <a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Beaufort,_Earl_of_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John Beaufort, Earl of Dorset (page does not exist)">John Beaufort, Earl of Dorset</a>, 1455\xe2\x80\x931471, died without issue</dd>\n<dd>g. Thomas Beaufort, 1455\xe2\x80\x931463, died young</dd></dl></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>G. <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">Cardinal</a> <a href="/wiki/Henry_Beaufort" title="Henry Beaufort">Henry Beaufort</a> <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Winchester" title="Bishop of Winchester">Bishop of Winchester</a>, 1375\xe2\x80\x931447, died without issue</dd>\n<dd>H. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Beaufort,_Duke_of_Exeter" title="Thomas Beaufort, Duke of Exeter">Thomas Beaufort, Duke of Exeter</a>, 1377\xe2\x80\x931427, had 1 son;\n<dl><dd>I. Henry Beaufort, died young</dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p><b>House of York</b><sup id="cite_ref-HoY_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoY-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd><dl><dd><dl><dd><dl><dd><dl><dd>5. <a href="/wiki/Edmund_of_Langley,_1st_Duke_of_York" title="Edmund of Langley, 1st Duke of York">Edmund of Langley, 1st Duke of York</a>, 1341\xe2\x80\x931402, had 2 sons;\n<dl><dd>A. <a href="/wiki/Edward_of_Norwich,_2nd_Duke_of_York" title="Edward of Norwich, 2nd Duke of York">Edward of Norwich, 2nd Duke of York</a>, 1373\xe2\x80\x931415, died without issue</dd>\n<dd>B. <a href="/wiki/Richard_of_Conisburgh,_3rd_Earl_of_Cambridge" title="Richard of Conisburgh, 3rd Earl of Cambridge">Richard of Conisburgh, 3rd Earl of Cambridge</a>, 1375\xe2\x80\x931415, had 1 son;\n<dl><dd>I. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Plantagenet,_3rd_Duke_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Plantagenet, 3rd Duke of York">Richard Plantagenet, 3rd Duke of York</a>, 1411\xe2\x80\x931460, had 8 sons;\n<dl><dd>a. Henry of York, 1441\xe2\x80\x931441, died in infancy</dd>\n<dd>b. <a href="/wiki/Edward_IV_of_England" title="Edward IV of England">Edward IV of England</a>, 1442\xe2\x80\x931483, had 3 sons and 7 daughters;\n<dl><dd>i. <a href="/wiki/Edward_V_of_England" title="Edward V of England">Edward V of England</a>, 1470\xe2\x80\x93?, died without issue</dd>\n<dd>ii. <a href="/wiki/Richard_of_Shrewsbury,_1st_Duke_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard of Shrewsbury, 1st Duke of York">Richard of Shrewsbury, 1st Duke of York</a>, 1473\xe2\x80\x93?, died without issue</dd>\n<dd>iii. <a href="/wiki/George_Plantagenet,_Duke_of_Bedford" class="mw-redirect" title="George Plantagenet, Duke of Bedford">George Plantagenet, Duke of Bedford</a>, 1477\xe2\x80\x931479, died young</dd>\n<dd>iv. <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_York" title="Elizabeth of York">Elizabeth of York</a> married <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a>, 4 sons and 4 daughters\n<dl><dd><b>To the House of Tudor</b></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>c. <a href="/wiki/Edmund,_Earl_of_Rutland" title="Edmund, Earl of Rutland">Edmund, Earl of Rutland</a>, 1443\xe2\x80\x931460, died without issue</dd>\n<dd>d. William of York, 1447\xe2\x80\x931447, died in infancy</dd>\n<dd>e. John of York, 1448\xe2\x80\x931448, died in infancy</dd>\n<dd>f. <a href="/wiki/George_Plantagenet,_1st_Duke_of_Clarence" title="George Plantagenet, 1st Duke of Clarence">George Plantagenet, 1st Duke of Clarence</a>, 1449\xe2\x80\x931478, had 2 sons and 2 daughters;\n<dl><dd>i. <a href="/wiki/Edward_Plantagenet,_17th_Earl_of_Warwick" title="Edward Plantagenet, 17th Earl of Warwick">Edward Plantagenet, 17th Earl of Warwick</a>, 1475\xe2\x80\x931499, died without issue</dd>\n<dd>ii. Richard of York, 1476\xe2\x80\x931477, died in infancy</dd>\n<dd>iii. <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Pole,_Countess_of_Salisbury" title="Margaret Pole, Countess of Salisbury">Margaret Pole, Countess of Salisbury</a>, 1473\xe2\x80\x931541, considered by some to be the last of the Plantagenets, had 4 sons and one daughter, considered the source of one of the <a href="/wiki/Alternative_successions_of_the_English_crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative successions of the English crown">Alternative successions of the English crown</a>.\n<dl><dd>A. <a href="/wiki/Henry_Pole,_1st_Baron_Montagu" title="Henry Pole, 1st Baron Montagu">Henry Pole, 1st Baron Montagu</a>\n<dl><dd><b>To the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Huntingdon" title="Earl of Huntingdon">Earl of Huntingdon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marquess_of_Hastings" title="Marquess of Hastings">Marquess of Hastings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Loudoun" title="Earl of Loudoun">Earl of Loudoun</a></b></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>g. Thomas of York, 1451\xe2\x80\x931451, died in infancy</dd>\n<dd>h. <a href="/wiki/Richard_III_of_England" title="Richard III of England">Richard III of England</a>, 1452\xe2\x80\x931485, had 1 son;\n<dl><dd>i. <a href="/wiki/Edward_of_Middleham,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Edward of Middleham, Prince of Wales">Edward of Middleham, Prince of Wales</a>, 1473\xe2\x80\x931484, died young</dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n</div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Plantagenet name is spelt in English sources in several ways, such as Plantaganet, Plantagenett, Plantagenette, Plantaginet, Plantagynett, etc.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For instance, David Crouch in <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.ie/books?id=Yb9cOQAACAAJ">William Marshal: Court, Career, and Chivalry in the Angevin Empire, 1147\xe2\x80\x931219</a></i> (Longman, 1990); Ralph V. Turner and Richard Heiser in <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.ie/books?id=62_JAwAAQBAJ&amp;">The Reign of Richard Lionheart: Ruler of The Angevin Empire, 1189\xe2\x80\x931199</a></i> (Routledge, 2000)</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Plantagenet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-plant2007-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-plant2007_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFPlant2007">Plant 2007</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFWagner2001">Wagner 2001</a>, p.&#160;206</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Wilson-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Wilson_4-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFKeefe2008">Keefe 2008</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFReference-OED-Angevin" class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://oed.com/search?searchType=dictionary&amp;q=Angevin">"Angevin"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i> (3rd ed.).
